AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
TITLE: MovableType Successfully Installed on Windows XP
STATUS: publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 1
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: Website
CATEGORY: Website

DATE: 09/11/2002 11:56:20 PM
-----
BODY:
To be honest, I don't know too much about Perl. However, to make the best weblog system work - <a href="http://www.movabletype.org">Movable Type</a>, I installed Perl onto my Windows XP machine from scretch. I believe I am not alone to install MT to Windows XP machines - although I believe there will not be too many people doing so - so I'd like to record the steps for other's reference. It is also a good resource for myself if I need to rebuild the server.

<b>Environment</b>
Windows XP
Inetnet Information Server (IIS)

<b>Install Perl on Windows XP</b>
<ul>
<li>Download ActivePerl for Windows XP from <a href="http://activestate.com/Products/Download/Register.plex?id=ActivePerl">ActiveState</a>. At the time I downloaed, the version was ActivePerl 5.6.1 build 633.
<li>After registering my user information, I choosed <a href="http://downloads.activestate.com/ActivePerl/Windows/5.6/ActivePerl-5.6.1.633-MSWin32-x86.msi">WIndows MSI package</a>, which is 8.31M in size.
<li>It took me about 2 minutes and 51 seconds to download - thanks to the broadband provider - <a href="http://www.gwbn.net.cn/">China Great Wall Broadband Corp</a>[Chinese site]. I haven't dreamed of downloading files larger than 5M in 10 minutes before.
<li>Install the MSI package. There is no any problem during the installation. I accepted all the defaul settings expect changing the default location from c:\Perl to c:\Program Files\Perl. I believe it is always good to follow the Windows convension instead of seeking for a place in root directory of C:\. This makes the disk hard to manage. <font color=red>Update</font> I am changing my mind recently. "C:\Program Files" folder is special in terms of Read-only settings and security permissions. Moving programs from their original location to this folder may bring unneccessary trouble if the program has never been tested in this environment.
</ul>

<b>Download MT source code</b>
<ul>
<li>Download the MT source code from <a href="http://www.movabletype.org/download.shtml">http://www.movabletype.org/download.shtml</a>. It is only 299K in size and took me 5 seconds to get it from the other side of the Pacific.
<li>Having MT-2.21.tar.gz on my disk, I met the first problem. I rely heavily on Windows XP to extract all .ZIP files and don't use WinZip any more, but it seems I need to get my Winzip back. OK. Download a trial version from <a href="http://download.com.com/3001-2250-8132587.html">www.winzip.com</a> and continue.
<li>Now all the source code is located in C:\Inetpub\Wwwroot\Mt folder, which can be accessed via http://home.wangjianshuo.com/mt. I am very serious about naming convensions. I cannot bear to put all the files directly into the root folder.
</ul>

<b>Configure IIS for Perl and perl script with .CGI extension to work</b>
<ul>
<li>I know it is wired for more green hand to have CGI run on Windows computer. At this time, if anyone access http://home.wangjianshuo.com/mt/mt.cgi, it will prompt to download the file instead of see the result. I configured IIS to recognize .CGI extension just as it recognize .ASP or .SHTML.
<li>In Inetmgr.exe, right click MT folder and select Properties. Click Create button in Application Settings area on Directory tab. Now we have created a seperate application.
<li>Click Configure and check the program to parse .pl files. It is <i>C:\program files\perl\bin\perl.exe "%s" %s</I> for my server.
<li>Note: The following changes can be changed on website level, no applicaiton level. Click Add and enter the same parsing program (<i>C:\program files\perl\bin\perl.exe "%s" %s</I> for my case) and enter .cgi to Extension text box. Click OK.
</ul>

<b>Configure MT to work on my site</b>
<ul>
<li>Open MT.cfg
<li>Changed the <b>CGIPath</b> to http://home.wangjianshuo.com/mt/
<li>Changed <b>DataSource</b> to c:\inetpub\wwwroot\mt\db\
</ul>

<font color=red>Updated</font>
<b>Install additional MT modules</b>

Before you can run your MovableType, you still need to install more required ActivePerl components. As stated in <a href="http://www.movabletype.org/docs/mtinstall.html#checking%20for%20perl%20modules">Checking for Perl Modules</a> section of MovableType Installation menual, you need to run <i>http://home.wangjianshuo.com/mt/mt-check.cgi</i>.

At the time I downloaded ActivePerl, it includes most of the required modules except the following:

<code>
    DB_File
    Image-Size
    HTML-template
</code>

Typically, you need to follow these steps:

1. Start -> Run
2. Type "cmd" and click "OK"
3. In DOS command line, enter "PPM" (without quotation marks) 
4. When PPM> prompt apprears, type "Install HTML-template" 
5. Wait until it is installed, then type "Install Image-Size"
6. Type "Install DB_File"
7. Quite PPM program.

Thanks for <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20020911_movabletype_successfully_installed_on_windows_xp.htm#comments85">Jeff</a> for pointing this out. I forgot to add this item before.

<font color=red>Updated again</font>
<b>Fail to Install DB_File</b>

If you see this error message when installing DB_File

<blockquote>PPM> Install DB_File
Install package 'DB_File?' (y/N): Y
Installing package 'DB_File'...
Error installing package 'DB_File': Read a PPD for 'DB_File', but it is not inte
nded for this build of Perl (MSWin32-x86-multi-thread)</blockquote>

You may try to follow the steps below:

<ul><li>Visit <a href="http://ppm.activestate.com/PPMPackages/zips/">http://ppm.activestate.com/PPMPackages/zips/</a>
<li>Choose 5.6.xxx or 5.5.xxxx from the list. Typically, you are running on 5.6.xxx. So you should be directed to this page <a href="http://ppm.activestate.com/PPMPackages/zips/6xx-builds-only/">http://ppm.activestate.com/PPMPackages/zips/6xx-builds-only/</a>
<li>Find and download DB_File.zip (<a href="http://ppm.activestate.com/PPMPackages/zips/6xx-builds-only/DB_File.zip">http://ppm.activestate.com/PPMPackages/zips/6xx-builds-only/DB_File.zip</a>)
<li>Unzip the file and put the extracted file to your local disk, for example, c:\temp\DB_File.ppd.
<li>In DOS command line, type <code>PPM Install c:\temp\DB_File.ppd</code></ul>

Thanks for Samuel Wan for <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20020911_movabletype_successfully_installed_on_windows_xp.htm#Comments154">pointing this out</a> for me. I have also wrote another blog entry on this: <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030131_db_file_error_when_installing_movabletype.htm#000153">DB_File Error When Installing MovableType</a>

<b>Complete the installation</b>
<ul>
<li>After all the steps are perfomed, there is very little work left. Just follow the <a href="http://www.movabletype.org/docs/mtinstall.html">installation instruction</a> and it works very well.
<li>The <a href="http://www.movabletype.org/docs/mtmanual.html">user manual</a> is also very good resource to go ahead to configure the MT system.
</ul>

<font color=red>Updated</font>
<b>Sending Email on Windows XP</b>

Sending email on Unix system seems easy. Just configure the sendmail command and it will work. Typically you don't have any SMTP server that you can configure MT to send to. To port MovableType on Windows system (Windows 2000 or Windows XP or Windows .NET Server), you will need to configure the SMTP services of IIS.

<ul><li>Check you have IIS install with SMTP service. Start -> Control Panel -> Add/Remove Programs -> Add/Remove Windows Component. (or simply Start -> Run -> AppWiz.cpl). Ensure IIS is selected. You may also want to click Details... button to see if SMTP is installed within IIS.
<li>Make sure SMTP is started. Start -> Run -> InetMgr.exe. Make sure SMTP is up and running.
<li>Configure On properity sheet of SMTP Viture Server, click Relay button on Access tab. The default setting is "Only the list below". Add the IP address of the server your MovableType is hosted to the list. Or, select "All expect the list below". The later one is not recommended since it may open a door for spammers to use your server to send spams. (Microsoft has more <a href="http://support.microsoft.com/default.aspx?scid=kb;en-us;Q308161">detailed articles</a> on configuration of SMTP Service.)
<li>Configure MovableType to send mail using local SMTP server. Uncomment the lines below in mt.cfg file.
<blockquote>MailTransfer smtp
SMTPServer wangjian.ipowermysql.com</blockquote>
Replace wangjian.ipowermysql.com with the host name of your SMTP server if you are hosting the servers on two machines.</ul>

Regarding the question, "why did you install perl into your Windows XP", it is a very good question. Why? First of all, I just installed broadband in my house with high speed and real and relatively static IP address. So I have a good reason in host my site on my own PC. Since the OS on my PC is already Windows XP Professional, after I decided I am going to use MT, I went to web and found ActivePerl and all the required component. I am lucky that I setup everything with one hour. It is also a feat to me. (I learnt the word "feat" from your post. I didn't know this word before - English is not my native language.)

COMMENT:
AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
EMAIL: jianshuo@hotmail.com
IP: 207.46.71.13
URL: http://home.wangjianshuo.com
DATE: 10/22/2002 02:27:21 PM
Hi Pagal,

Thanks for writing comment to my blog. 

First of all, I need to disclaim that
a) I am not familiar with Perl, as I stated in the first sentence of this blog entry.
b) I may not be able to help you to troubleshoot this strange problem since I just used the steps listed and it works like a charm. So I didn't met this problem.

After you read the disclaimer, I will try to give you my immediate suggestion.

1) Please make sure c:\inetpub\wwwroot\blog folder is there before you try to rebuild. Based on my experience (may not be right), MovableType will NOT create folder for you. You need to create the folder "blog" by yourself before rebuild. I believe this is the most possible cause of the problem.

2) Have you tried use the default path, that is, use c:\inetpub\wwwroot to store the archives?

3) If the step 2 does not work too, please check the Security setting of c:\inetpub\wwwroot. For troubleshooting propose, set it to be EVERYONE Full Control (Right click -> Properties -> Security tabe -> Add -> Everyone -> Check Full control -> OK) If this works, it should be security reason. Please note that setting everyone full control to the folder is only for testing propose. Remain this setting may cause security holes of your server.

If it still does not solve the problem, I suggest you post the question into MovableType's Support Forum at <a href="http://www.movabletype.org/cgi-bin/ikonboard/ikonboard.cgi">http://www.movabletype.org/cgi-bin/ikonboard/ikonboard.cgi</a> . Maybe somebody there has encountered the same problem as you and can help you.

Jian Shuo

AUTHOR: Samuel Wan

DATE: 01/04/2003 12:52:47 PM
I have been trying to install MT on my Windows 2000 server for a very long time. The biggest problem came from trying to install the DB_File module!

After much searching, I came across this website: "<a href="http://misterhouse.net/install.html",">http://misterhouse.net/install.html",</a> which mentions a similar difficulty installing the db_file module. The webpage walks through the installation of activeperl 5.8 (or higher), and describes the following steps:

> cd \perl\bin (modify to match your directory)
   > ppm
   ppm > repository add <a href="http://theoryx5.uwinnipeg.ca/cgi-bin/ppmserver?urn:/PPMServer58">http://theoryx5.uwinnipeg.ca/cgi-bin/ppmserver?urn:/PPMServer58</a>
   ppm> install GD
   ppm> install DB_File

Now, I've tried typing "install DB_file" many times without success, but I successfully installed DB_File after adding the repository and installing the GD module first.

I love movable type, and hope that this post will help others who have experienced problems with ActivePerl and DB_File

-Samuel Wan

COMMENT:
AUTHOR: Evgeny
EMAIL: fadeev@rocketmail.com
IP: 128.112.81.53
URL: 
DATE: 01/19/2003 09:26:28 AM
hello

i had the same problem
check if libdb.dll (active perl usually puts it in C:\Perl\bin)
is in the system path.
On XP(and maybe NT) go to settings->control panel->system->advanced
click Environment variables and append
;C:\Perl\bin (or whatever in your case)
to _system_ (not user) PATH
apache does not run scripts under your name by default

i hope it helps

DB_File windows DB_File.pm libdb.dll "Can't load"

COMMENT:
AUTHOR: Byron
EMAIL: nospam@fuckspam.com
IP: 24.74.226.199
URL: 
DATE: 03/17/2003 12:46:25 PM
Hi again,

I just got it all installed and setup properly.  Thanks to Jian Shuo Wang and Deane Barker for the info on your sites and various postings on the subject (at MT help forums too).  

It took me two whole days to get it running on WinXP/Apache2/Perl5.8/MySQL3.23.55.  The problem I had was that for some reason, mt-check.cgi (mt-check.pl for win32) and mt-load.cgi (mt-load.pl for win32) did not work when called from a web browser (<a href="http://wangjian.ipowermysql.com/mt/mt-check.pl,">http://wangjian.ipowermysql.com/mt/mt-check.pl,</a> <a href="http://wangjian.ipowermysql.com/mt/mt-load.pl).">http://wangjian.ipowermysql.com/mt/mt-load.pl).</a>  

I finally figured out that they ran just fine from the WinXP command line, and that I had DBI::mysql and ImageMagick configured just fine the whole time.  Actually I did get a popup error that Perl56.dll could not be found when running at the command line, but I just ignored it b/c I'm using Perl58.dll, and b/c it otherwise worked correctly and returned the correct results in the command line.  

Anyway, once I ran "perl mt-load.cgi" from the command line, I could then browse to <a href="http://wangjian.ipowermysql.com/mt/mt.pl">http://wangjian.ipowermysql.com/mt/mt.pl</a> and that worked.

Also, adding e:\mysql\bin to WinXP PATH was necessary too.

Thanks again for the help everyone.

PS - I'm running MT on wangjian.ipowermysql.com just to experiment and learn, I don't have any plans to put it on a public site anytime soon.
-----

TITLE: Campus Network Application Needed for China Universities
STATUS: publish

ALLOW PINGS: 0

BODY:
10:09 PM

Recently, I am involved in the discussion with some students from <a href="http://www.ecnu.edu.cn/">East China Normal University</a>[Chinese site]. Most of them are computer science or related majors. Billy Qiu is one of them. He is a talented guy who actively initialized the MSN Messenger chat with me the day before yesterday.

After we discussed, the technical club members are going to setup some interest groups on campus to discuss technology trends and share technical resources. 

Actually this is a very good idea, just as <a href="http://www.apple.com/usergroups/">Apple's User Group</a> and <a href="http://www.ineta.org/">Internet .NET Associate</a>, the local interest groups will highly help the participants to learn technologies.

During our discussion on the proposals, Billy also shared some concerns.
<blockquote>
"They (the students) dont like to do logistics & admin work. What they really care, and really interested is just the core technology. Knowing about the GAME rule, following the rule, making proposal, and calling group meetings... etc are very boring, they think." Billy said.
</blockquote>

I fully understand Billy's concern. It reminded me about the time when I was in <a href="http://www.sjtu.edu.cn">Shanghai Jiaotong University</a>[Chinese site]. It is back to 1995-1999. At that time, Internet access is not popular and there is very few resources on intranet. It changes greatly recently. Take a look at Shanghai Jiao Tong University:
<ul>
<li>Students dorms are connected with LANs. 
<li>BBS is more popluar (it has been popular since 1993) (See <a href="http://bbs.sjtu.edu.cn">SJTU BBS</a>[Chinese site])
<li>Students are enjoying movies on campus network
</ul>
Despit all this improvement, the campus of nowadays in China are still far behind the pace of global IT in terms of electronic communications. I'd like to see some students on campus really think hard and think out of box, inspire others with the possibility IT may bring to their lives.

A lot of powerful tools has been avaiable for online collaboration. For example, <a href="http://www.blogger.co">Blogger</a>, or knowledge managemetn tools such as <a href="http://www.microsoft.com/frontpage/sharepoint/">SharePoint Team Services</a>, and other online collaboration tools are very good for use on campus. During the process of implementation, students will learn a lot.
<blockquot>
If I have to learn something, I learn it by doing.
-Arstoter
</blockquot>
My thoughts for all the borthers
<ul>
<li><b>Knowing about the GAME rule</b> - Good thing is, IT can help to greatly simplify the game rule. Just check project like <a href="http://www.zeal.com">zeal.com</a>, which used the system to simplified the contribution, review, and publish process. No one need to bother to learn the details of the rules. <a href="http://www.dmoz.org">Open Directory Project</a> is another successful colloration project.
<li><b>Following the rule</b> - IT system is will do the logisitic work for you.
<li><b>Making proposal</b> - sorry, you need to do this party
<li><b>Calling group meetings...</b> - Why bother call so many meetings? Online collaration will do most of the job
</ul>
Later, I found there is no <b>classroom reservation system</b>, which can be used to reserve classrooms electronicly. There is no <b>online libary services</b>, which will help to deliver the book you want to your dorm. There is very large space there. I will keep my eyes on their progress and I'd like to see them make great impact using the technologies.

Good luck

<i>Please check Comments below to share your thoughts on the possibilities IT will change students lives.</i>

AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
TITLE: Network Infrustucture in my Home in Shanghai
STATUS: publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 1
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: Shanghai
CATEGORY: Shanghai

DATE: 09/13/2002 10:33:11 PM
-----
BODY:
11:50 PM

I have been asked about how I can access Internet. For friends in Shanghai, they are curious about the broadband, which is new to the city.

<b>Dial-up:</b> Basically, residents in Shanghai have lots of choices for Internet access from home. 
<ul>
<li>The China Telecom is the largest and most popular provider of dial-up access.
<blockquote>Telephone #: 8163
username: 8163
password: 8163</blockquote>

The Internet service fee will be charged to the caller's telephone bill. This is very convenience. We don't need to apply a user account. (What about other regions in the world? Writhe comments and let us hear you.)
<li>Their there many other ISPs are providing Internet Access card. Users buy the cards and can dial the number on the card for predefined period of Internet Access time. It is also good and cheaper than 8163 service.
</ul>

<b>Broadband</b>

There are many service providers are competing to gain more market share here in Shanghai
<ul><li>China Telecom is selling <a href="http://www.howstuffworks.com/dsl.htm">ADSL</a> - the method to use normal telephone line to transmit digital signals, though greatly speed-up the data transition.
<li>Cable TV providers are persuading users to use <a href="http://www.howstuffworks.com/cable-modem.htm">cable modem</a> to access Internet.
<li>China Unicom, which don't have the fixed line telephone are using wireless technology to gain its market. User with wireless LAN adaptor can subscribe to their services.
<li>Other broadband providers like Great Wall Broadband - the provider I chose. They are using traditional LAN technologies for users in a residential area. 
</ul>

Let me share some facts of the broadband I am using.

<b>Speed</b> The inbound network cable provides 100M access to other servers on the LAN, and provide pretty good Internet access rate (not very sure about the exact bandwidth now) I tried to <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20020911_movabletype_successfully_installed_on_windows_xp.htm">download some files</a>, the transfer rate displayed on downloading dialog box is typically 40 KB/sec to 100 KB/sec.

<b>IP address</b> GWBN is providing dynamic, real IP address.

<ul><li><i>Dynamic IP</i> GWBN uses DHCP to allocate IP addresses on a LAN. Heroically, the IP may change. However, because currently the number of subscribers is far less than number of IPs in the IP pool, the IP addresses for my computers never changed. So I can safely direct my domain <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com">http://home.wangjianshuo.com</a> to my IP address <a href="http://211.161.107.18">211.161.107.18</a>.
<li><i>Real IP</i> Unlike China Telecom broadband and other broadband who are using NAT (<a href="http://www.howstuffworks.com/nat.htm">Network Address Translation</a>), GWBN provides  real IP address. I queried my IP address 211.161.107.18 in <a href="http://www.apnic.net">www.apnic.net</a>, the <a href="http://www.apnic.net/apnic-bin/whois.pl?searchtext=211.161.107.18">result</a> looks like this
<blockquote>inetnum:      211.161.107.0 - 211.161.107.255
netname:      GWBN-SH-COMMUNITY145
descr:        FOR GWBN SHANGHAI # 145 RESIDENTIAL COMMUNITY BROADBAND NETWORK USERS' BROADBAND ACCESS
country:      CN
admin-c:      JM97-AP
tech-c:       JM97-AP
mnt-by:       MAINT-CNNIC-AP
changed:      mengjian@gwbn.net.cn 20020715
status:       ALLOCATED PORTABLE
source:       APNIC
</blockquote>
I guess the so-called "# 145 RESIDENTIAL COMMUNITY" refers to Vanke Waltz Garden. That means 773 families are sharing the 255 IP addresses. It is pretty good, since only about 5% of the residents are subscribers now.

I randomly checked some IP from <a href="http://www.apnic.net/apnic-bin/whois.pl?searchtext=211.161.0.18">211.161.0.18</a> to <a href="http://www.apnic.net/apnic-bin/whois.pl?searchtext=211.161.253.18">211.161.253.18</a> and found them all belong to GWBN. It seems the company has lots of IP addresses for the broadband services.

Broadband is becoming more and more popular here in big cities like Beijing and Shanghai. I am enjoying the high speed of the broadbands provide. However, it is still far behind the market's expectation. Millions of dolloars have been put into the infrastructure construction, but the output is disappointing. According to media, most broadband providers are having a hard time now. For providers like GWBN, the situation is even worse. According to recent media report, GWBN needs about 500 million RMB for its daily operation, while it only receives less than 50 million RMB from its subscribers.

About months ago, GWBN announced to be transformed into a content provider instead of Internet Service Provider. Source: <a href="http://www.gwbn.net.cn/news/gwbn/20020913/200209131.htm">http://www.gwbn.net.cn/news/gwbn/20020913/200209131.htm</a> [Chinese site]

To Bethune:

Sorry for late answering your questions. For the 8163 service, people get detailed bill for that. It is combined with the telecom's telephone bill. In the bill, there is a column named "information services". That record the cost of the 8163 Internet services.

For 8163, it is dial-up Internet services and it is charged by minute (about 0.4 RMB or something like that per minute)

For broadband, most of them provide "all-you-can-eat" package. It costs 100 RMB for Greatwall Broadband and 130 RMB for ADSL Broadband Access. There is no limitation on connected time or bandwith limitation.

There are other options for cheaper access with bandwidth limitation. It really depends on the service provider. The good thing is, there are too many choices for end users and you can always pick the right one for you.

AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
TITLE: ODP - Not As Good as Zeal.com
STATUS: publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 1
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: Website
CATEGORY: Website

DATE: 09/14/2002 09:31:48 PM
-----
BODY:
... or my experience of becoming an ODP (<a href="http://dmoz.org">Open Directory Project</a>) editor.

Inspired by andersja's <a href="http://www.jacobsen.no/anders/blog/archives/2002/08/08/optimizing_movable_type_part_3_get_more_readers.html">Optimizing Movable Type (part 3) - get more readers </a>, I sent my blog site to DMOZ.org.

<blockquote>While you're there - consider signing up as an editor: it's easy to sign up, there are lots of tools available for you to do your editing, and loads of support to be had from other editors. -- andersja </blockquote>

This is a cool idea, so I signed up today to be an editor of <a href="http://dmoz.org/Regional/Asia/China/Provinces_and_Regions/Henan/Luoyang/">http://dmoz.org/Regional/Asia/China/Provinces_and_Regions/Henan/Luoyang/</a> catalog. This is the city I was born and I'd like to help to build up the portal. It is strange that there is only two sites listed under this category.

I am interested in <a href="http://www.useit.com">usability</a> analysis recently and tend to review the usibility of all web site I come across. This is no exception this time - I found it easy to locate the link of "Become an editor". However, it is confusing that the notice of "This category needs an editor" are seperate from the Adverstisement of "Become an editor". Why not merge them together by simply say "This category needs an editor. Apply now." with hyper link of application form?

For the application form, it seems normal, like thousands of similar pages. However, I am quite confused by the <a href="http://dmoz.org/cgi-bin/apply.cgi?submit=Proceed&where=Regional%2FAsia%2FChina%2FProvinces_and_Regions%2FHenan%2FLuoyang&id=&lk=&loc=">section</a> to submit 2 or 3 URLs. This is the road-block to submit my review form. What I am going to do is to submit a review form so I can continue to contribute to the community, but the form designer may thing I must have prepared everything and be ready for this question. To continue, I have to grasp some sites very quickly and submitted it. To be honest, I think the quality shown by these three samples are not the quality I will contribute. It is much lower, since I was not concentrated on that. 

<b>How to improve?</b>

There should be seperated into two steps. The first step, you register a user name and password, so you can become a candidate in the database immediately. Later, in order to get reviewed to become an editor, you have plenty of time to come back to complete the <a href="http://dmoz.org/cgi-bin/apply.cgi?submit=Proceed&where=Regional%2FAsia%2FChina%2FProvinces_and_Regions%2FHenan%2FLuoyang&id=&lk=&loc=">sample URL question</a>. This makes more sense.

<b>Zeal.com is doing a better job</b>

<a href="http://zeal.com">Zeal.com</a> is doing the same thing as DMOZ.org. Zeal obviously knows better about community then its competitors. Zeal.com does not only judge whether you are qualified to become a contributor or editor, it also help you to learn and become qualified. The Zeal.com provide <a href="http://zeal.com/guidelines/user/">guidelines</a> to educate community members to write good descriptions and put sites into the right categories. It also setup the mechanism for peer-to-peer review. The quality quotient reflect the qualify of a contributor, which helps to improve the overall quality of the dictionary.

<blockquote>"Listing may take anything from 2 weeks to several months, so once you've submitted, just try to forget about the whole thing... ;-)" andersja said</blockquote>

I cannot agree with you more on that. Submission for free or volunteer based communities should never be too serious. Just submit and forget. It will make life much easier.
-----

Consider to become an ODP (dmoz.org) editor? It seems not easy. Comparsion between Zeal.com and Dmoz.org let me choose Zeal.com

AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
TITLE: Korea: The Bandwitdh Capital of the World?
STATUS: publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 1
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: Misc
CATEGORY: Misc

DATE: 09/15/2002 11:14:43 PM
-----
BODY:
Today, I found this piece of news about broadband in Korea. This is one of my interest recently. Please read this first.

<A HREF="http://www.wired.com/wired/archive/10.08/korea.html">In Seoul, the broadband age is in full swing - online games have become a national sport, and cybercafes are the new singles bars.</A>

<Blockquote>And the numbers are impressive ?South Korea has the highest per capita broadband penetration in the world. <b>Slightly more than half of its households have high-bandwidth connections</b>, compared to less than 10 percent in the US. The growth in broadband has surged in the last three years from a few hundred thousand subscribers to 8.5 million</blockquote>

<Blockquote>As luck would have it, urban apartment dwellers have a lot of broadband capacity right under their noses, courtesy of Kepco, the public power utility, which developed a network of fiber-optic cables for its own use years ago. In 1996, South Korea allowed Kepco to lease the unused 90 percent of its capacity, giving upstart providers a cheap, instant last-mile solution. Sharp competition with Korea Telecom, which the government forced to open its network in the early '90s, has driven broadband prices down to the world's lowest levels. All-you-can-eat service is available for as little as $25 a month. </Blockquote>

I partly disagree with the report on some details.

<b>South Korea has the highest per capita broadband penetration in the world? No.</b>

According to <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2002/TECH/08/20/hln.wired.cities/">Nielsen/NetRatings report</a>, Hong Kong seems to be the top region in the world, with amazing 66.6% of people accessing Internet using broadband. German 45%, Switherland 43%.... United States ranked low with 17% broadband access, not less than 10%.

<b>... drives broadband prices down to the world's lowest level? Maybe.</b>

It is true that it is of the world's lowest level, but it is not the lowest price in the world. In Shanghai, ADSL (type of DSL) charges 130 RMB ($15.7) each month. For 100M broadband, like GWBN, it costs only 100 RMB ($12) for one month.

<b>Korea did great job in broadband deployment? Yes.</b>

It is amazing to see how Korea is wired with broadband. The online game, PC Baangs, and the certification for buildings.... all sound exciting.

<b>Much more problems ahead for broadband deployment in Shanghai</b>

I checked local media to find the comparasion data in Shanghai. At last, I found this one:

<blockquote>Internet users in Shanghai exceeded one million last week. 61.7% in urban area chose traditional dial-up, the other 38.3% chose broadband.
source: <a href="http://tech.sina.com.cn/i/c/2002-09-10/0903137687.shtml">Jie Fang Daily</a> (Chinese site)</blockquote>

However, the situation here is not that good than in Korea. Another report from <a href="http://eastday.com">Eastday.com</a> (Chinese site), only 5% of the residents are subscribers of broadband. News about the finanical difficulties for some broadband companies is full of media.

AUTHOR: Bill

COMMENT:
AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
EMAIL: jianshuo@hotmail.com
IP: 211.161.107.4
URL: http://www.wangjianshuo.com
DATE: 09/16/2002 08:18:15 PM
It is a very good question. Actually, I shoud describe this in more details in the article. 

GWBN uses traditional LAN technology to provide access to Internet. It typically install a 100M switch for each building, which means the inbound network cable has the capacity of 100M. If you access servers on the same LAN, and some local resources, you have the speed of 100M. This is what I call 100M GWBN. It is very high speed comparied with other offers like DSL, which is 512K. Of cause when access Internet web site which typically not on the high speed LAN, the speed will be limited by the connection between the site and the LAN.
-----

AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
TITLE: I was a Called Copier Today
STATUS: publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 1
ALLOW PINGS: 1
PRIMARY CATEGORY: Website
CATEGORY: Website

DATE: 09/17/2002 12:33:51 AM

BODY:
Today, I was shocked when I found my name appreared on my favorite weblog <a href="http://www.jacobsen.no/anders/blog/archives/2002/09/16/imitation_is_the_most_sincere_form_of_flattery.html">andersja's blog</a>. It is even more astonishing when I found my name was related to something negative - copier.

<blockquote>"I like writing articles and other content for my weblog, and I like tinkering with design - visually and technically. Now, wangjianshuo has copied my CSS stylesheet and also other MT config elements very closely, and I'm not entirely sure if I'm comfortable with it. 

Other people occationally nab links without linking back... not exactly weblog etiquette, but something we'll have to live with...?"

andersja wrote.</blockquote>

I have to say, it is my fault not to be careful enough to link back to the site I copied from or inspired by for all instances. However, I did link back in some blogs. 

<i>I have changed my site after I saw andersja's post. For some of my readers of page was directed by the post, I still keep a <a href="http://www.wangjianshuo.com/news/20020916andersj/">copy</a> of my original page, so you know what andersja said is true.</I>

I wrote a <a href="http://www.jacobsen.no/anders/blog/archives/2002/09/16/imitation_is_the_most_sincere_form_of_flattery.html">comment</a> to clarify the whole thing. This is the comment I posted with a little bit change to add hyperlink to words instead of leaving the unclickable URLs.

<blockquote>Hi andersja,

This is Jian Shuo Wang, the “copier?you mentioned in your blog.

== Firstly, I apologize ==

First of all, I have to admit that I have used your CSS completely and I added category link function as you did on your site. I sincerely apologize for it since it has made your feel uncomfortable.

== But the true is, I did link back ==

You may misunderstand me on linking-back. The truth is, I did link back.

On my first blog at <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20020911_movabletype_successfully_installed_on_windows_xp.htm">MovableType Successfully Installed on Windows XP</a>, at the end, in the Acknowledge section, I wrote:

"I also want to thank andersja, the owner of anderrsja's blog. His site on weblog are very well done. I learnt a lot on categories and the pertential usage of MovableType from his site."

Certainly I swear I did it on the day of Sept 11 instead of adding it after you got angry. Geo, my friend at <a href="http://www.russianlegs.com">http://russianlegs.com</a> can also confirm it, since he also commented after my blog.

In the acknowledgement part, I mentioned the categories function on your web site. It inspired me a lot and I decided to make my own category links. I finally completed the function on the day before yesterday with the help with <a href=" http://www.movabletype.org/docs/mtmanual_tags.html#categoryrelated%20tags">MovableType document</a>.

I noticed you may have read this article since you wrote comment for this blog on the same day -- Sept 11, 2002 09:48 PM:

"Thanks for your feedback and congratulations with getting Movable Type running on XP - very cool (I haven't seen it done before :-) 

Happy blogging!

Posted by: andersja on September 11, 2002 09:48 PM?

Maybe you didn't notice I linked you back on my first blog.

== More evidence that I did link back ==

On my <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20020914_odp_not_as_good_as_zealcom.htm">forth blog</a>, I started my paragraph with

"Inspired by andersja's Optimizing Movable Type (part 3) - get more readers , I sent my blog site to DMOZ.org."

Posted by Jian Shuo Wang at September 14, 2002 09:31 PM | Categories: MovableType 

As you can see, as a beginer of blogging (only 6 logs so far), I have read carefully on many of your articles on your site and was trying to follow your steps to setup a blog. This includes registering my blog on DMOZ.org. But after I did, I wrote in my blog to thank andersj for the great inspiration you gave me.

I wrote six blogs so far and two of them mentioned that I am inspired by your site. I didn't put you on a seperate link for your site on the right pane of my first page. The only reason is, I am running this blog for less than one week and there is too much things for me to improve. I am going to do so now.

== The facts ==

I have commented on <a href="http://www.jacobsen.no/anders/blog/archives/2002/09/11/trillian_10_trillianpro_also_features_rss_newsreader.html">your page</a> on  and received your quick reply. This is very helpful for me. Although I have been web developer for many years, it is the first time I setup blog and the first time to play with Perl and MT stuff (as I mentioned at the beginning of my <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20020911_movabletype_successfully_installed_on_windows_xp.htm">first blog</a>. I worked very hard to get some idea from other great site like yours. I was using MT's default CSS template. I just wanted to change the font to Verdana instead of the odd font. At that time, I copied your CSS and made very little modification and used it in my site. 

== Anyway, I apologize ==

Again, I admit I did it. I should have mentioned somewhere on my blog, but I haven't yet. That is "not exactly weblog etiquette". I will go back to change it to the default one immediately if this made you uncomfortable.

Please be assured that I am not "fighting back" in this comment. I am still grateful for everything you did on your site, including sharing your setup experience of MT and your tips to optimizing MT. They inspired me a lot. That is the source of my first blog "MovableType Successfully Installed on Windows XP" and later, "Webcam Set Up, Broadcasting Shanghai". I will also continue to share how I created the site and how to make things work as you did. I agree with you weblog etiquette is very important and I am always trying my best to follow. Sometimes I may make mistakes and I will be fully responsible for that.

Please do not hesitate to let me know if any of my content or behavior makes you think I do not respect other people on the net. I'd like to hear and like to improve.

Best wishes
Jian Shuo Wang
The Copier</blockquote>

As always, Anders <a href="http://www.jacobsen.no/anders/blog/archives/2002/09/16/imitation_is_the_most_sincere_form_of_flattery.html">replied </a>very soon after I posted my comment. I agree with him on this reply:

<blockquote>To copy from one = plagiarism
To copy from many = inspiration! ;-)</blockquote>

I continued to send email to him and explain the whole story. It seems the mistake has been recovered and the issue has been settled.

<b>More on credibility</b>

Anders is a very kind guy who wrote this only to encourage innovation instead of plagiarism. This reminded me to check throughout my site to ensure I "<a href="http://www.spartaneity.com/02/08/honesty_credibility_revisited.html">properly give credit where credit is due</a>". It is essential to build up the credibility of the site I own.

<i>I was refered to this page by <a href="http://www.jacobsen.no/anders/blog/archives/2002/09/16/imitation_is_the_most_sincere_form_of_flattery.html">andersja's page</a>. After that, I found <a href="http://www.spartaneity.com/">Spartaneity Project</a> is a very good source for <a href="http://www.spartaneity.com/02/08/on_credibility.html">credibility</a>. </I>

<b>Result of the review</b>

After carefully reviewing the content of <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com">my site</a>, I found I did something good and something bad.

<ul><li>I kept the POWERED BY MOVABLE TYPE 2.21 logo which gave credit for MovableType. They did wonderful job on authoring this tool.
<li>I missed links-back on my homepage. I added link back under a special section called "Credits" on my homepage for <a href="http://www.jacobsen.no/anders/blog/">andersja's blog</a> and Geo's <a href="http://www.russianlegs.com">www.russianlegs.com</a>. Geo's site is the first one which let me be aware of the personal publishing form called "weblog" and andersja inspired me a lot on feature-related or technical aspect.
<li>It seems I have tried my best to keep giving credit. I gave credit to Billy Qiu when <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20020912_campus_network_application_needed_for_china_universities.htm">quoting his words</a> - I also asked him to review the page during the course of my publishing. 
<li>I linked to the source of the news in my blog on <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20020915_korea_the_bandwitdh_capital_of_the_world.htm">Korea's broadband development</a> and other sources.</ul>

To be honest, I didn't realize it is so important to add link to sources before this accident. I used it to make it easy to verify accuracy of the information of my site. Now it means something more important to me - to show respect to others by giving others credit. This is the most easy and powerful way to build up my own credit.
-----
EXTENDED BODY:

EXCERPT:
I was called copier today by my favorite weblog author, andersja, on his site. I explained that I am not that bad by show evidence - I did link back when inspired by his site. However, this is a very good lesson for me to really pay more attention on giving credit and build up own credit for doing it. All of us should do so, whenever it is online or offline.

AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
TITLE: Real-Time Stream Broadcasting Cookbook
STATUS: publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 1
ALLOW PINGS: 1
PRIMARY CATEGORY: Website
CATEGORY: Website

DATE: 09/18/2002 11:55:54 PM
-----
BODY:
9:50 PM

As I <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20020916_webcam_set_up_broadcasting_shanghai.htm">promised</a> before, I will share the steps how to set up a webcam to broadcast real time video with you in this article.

Before I begin, please visit my <a href="http://www.wangjianshuo.com/news/20020814WebCam/webcam.htm" target="_blank">webcam page</a> to experience what you are going to create. It will open a new window.

<b>Overview</b>

I am using Samsung Webcam + Windows XP Professional + Windows Media Encoder 9 Series 

<b>Client side platform supported</b>

Your experience will depend on the operating system you are using.
<ul><li><b>Windows XP</b>. You should not encounter with any problem if you are using Windows XP, since it includes Windows Media Player <a href="http://microsoft.com/windows/windowsmedia/default.asp">Windows Media Player</a> 8.0. <li><b>Windows 2000</b>. If you are using Windows 2000, which includes Windows Media 7.1, you will be prompted to install Windows Media 8.0 <a href="http://searchnetworking.techtarget.com/sDefinition/0,,sid7_gci211810,00.html">codec</a>. Choose Yes if you want to continue to view.
<li><b>Windows 98, Windows 95</b> I haven't tried yet, but it should be more complex to get it work. It includes Windows Media Player 6.4 by default.
<li><b>Mac</b>. If you cannot view it, try download <a href="http://microsoft.com/windows/windowsmedia/software/Macintosh/osx/default.asp">Windows Media Player for Mac OS X</a>. To be honest, I haven't tried to view my broadcasting on a Mac computer now.
<li><b>Solaris</b> <a href="http://microsoft.com/windows/windowsmedia/download/solaris.asp">Download Windows Media Player 6.3 for Solaris</a>. I was working of Solaris when I was in Tele cooperation Lab when I was a senior in SJTU. But I believe not so many people is using Solaris now, especially for viewing online media.
<li><b>Other OS</b>. I don't know how to view it. :-(
</ul> 

<b>Bandwidth required</b>

I am using broadband in my home. You should also use a high speed connection. I have tested it from different locations around China. It works very good for both broadband connection or T1.  My friend Bill Lum also told me that he can view the video smoothly in San Francisco. For modem dial-up, maybe you can only see black window, with "buffering" always there on status bar. Try a faster connection.

<b>Troubleshooting when connecting</b>

The correct status bar sequence should be

<ul><li><i>Connecting...</i>
<li><i>Connecting to Media...</i>
<li><i>Buffering: xx% complete...</i>
<li><i>Buffering: 100% complete...</i>
<li><I>Playing</i>
</ul>

If you see <i>Ready</i> in status bar but the video does not come out, it means there is connection problem. 
If you can see <i>Buffer</i>, it is speed problem.

<b>Hurry, tell me how you made it </B>

<ul><b>Hardware</b>: A normal computer that can run Windows XP is fine. Mine is a Intel Celeron 440, 256M Memory. Pretty low configured, isn’t it?
<b>OS</b>: I am using Windows XP. Windows 2000 will also do.
<b>Webcam</b>: Any webcam should be fine. I am using <a href="http://www.sem.samsung.com/product/anycam/products/descrip_c10.htm">Samsung Anycam</a>. The only annoying thing I met was, Windows does not natively support it, so I need to download <a href="http://www.sem.samsung.com/product/anycam/download/mlist.jsp">driver</a> separately for it.
<b>Media Server</b>: Broadcasting from home does not need a Windows Media Server, the only software you need is Windows Media Encoder. It is FREE. You can download the latest version from Microsoft <a href="http://www.microsoft.com/windows/windowsmedia/wm7/encoder.asp">web site</a>.</ul>

<b>Configure Windows Media Encoder</b>

After you download Windows Media Encoder (4.4 MB) and connect your Webcam with your computer, you can begin to setup your own TV station.

Follow the New Session Wizard. It should be very easy step, since more of the questions are easy to understand. Here are some tips:

<ul><li>Select "Broadcast a live event..." since you are not broadcasting a piece of video you have recorded.
<li>Select the camera in Video source.
<li>You can select your Audio source too, but don't expect the sound effect is good. You can use a .WAV file as background music.
<li>HTTP port. Just leave it as it was -- 8080. Change it if you have to.
<li>Always select Pull instead of Push, since you don't have <a href="http://www.microsoft.com/windows/windowsmedia/compare/webservvstreamserv.asp">Windows Media Server</a>.
<li>For profile selection, you can try different profile that meet your needs. The common rule is, the higher the resolution is, the more bandwidth it requires. I am using 320x240 in size, 15 fps, and on 100 kbps.
<li>Think carefully when entering Title and Author, it will be displayed on the viewer's media player.
<li>Finally, do NOT select save the video to file unless the video is really important or you have enough disk space.
</ul>

After everything is done, click "Start Encoding". Congratulations. The server part is done.

<b>How about the client then?</b>

To test, you can open Windows Media Player, click Open URL... on the File menu. In the "Open URL..." dialog box, enter your media source like this,

<blockquote>http://home.wangjianshuo.com:8080</blockquote>

(It is valid source and you can try to open it)

Substitute the source with your server name and the port you chose. 

If you can see the video, you can go ahead to create a web page so others can directly view it on a web page as <a href="http://www.wangjianshuo.com/news/20020814WebCam/webcam.htm">I did</a>.

You can copy the <a href="view-source:http://www.wangjianshuo.com/news/20020814WebCam/webcam.htm">source code</a> of my page into your page. You are free to do so and you don't need to link back since I got the source code from <a href="http://msdn.microsoft.com">MSDN sample</a>.

<b>Congratulations</b>

If you have successfully setup your own Windows Media server and can broadcast to the Internet, I will congratulate you on the achievement. I will feel very happy for the 1.5 hour I have spent on this article. <b>My only requirement for you is to write a comment under this article and share the URL of your online broadcasting station with my readers.</b>

<b>"Oops. It does not work as you said"</b>

It may also be common. Write a comment under this article so all the community members, including me, can help you on that.

Happy broadcasting!

<font color=red>Updated</font>

<ul><li>I am happy that Joe setup his cam using steps listed in this article. Thanks for <a href="http://24.229.158.77:8080/links.htm">linking</a> back. See <a href="http://24.229.158.77:8080/">his cam</a> <i>Nov 24, 2002</i></ul>

-----
EXTENDED BODY:

-----
EXCERPT:
This is a step-by-step guide for you to setup your own live broadcasting server in your home. After then, you can view the street outside your window, your children or pets in your house, any time, from any where. It is very cool, and it is very easy to setup.

AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
TITLE: From Pu Dong Airport to People's Park
STATUS: publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 1
ALLOW PINGS: 1
PRIMARY CATEGORY: Shanghai
CATEGORY: Shanghai

DATE: 09/19/2002 11:12:00 PM

BODY:
Today, I got a question from my reader:

<blockquote>Are there any reasonably priced shuttle services to get me from Shanghai Pudong airport to my hotel near Peoples Park?</blockquote>

It must be a very frequently asked question. Unfortunately, it is not easy to get an answer -- I checked on the web but couldn't find any useful resource before I gave up after five minutes. 

Here is my suggestion:

The most convienit and cheap way to get from Pu Dong Airport to anywhere in the dowtown is to go by the <a href="http://www.wangjianshuo.com/personal/places/pudongairport/Bus.htm">Airport Bus</a>. There are five lines connecting Pu Dong and downtown Shanghai.

<table border="1" bordercolor="#000000" style="border-collapse: collapse" cellpadding="5" cellspacing="0">
<th>#</td><td><b>From</b></td><td><b>To</b></td><td><b>Price (RMB) /Estm. USD
</b>
<tr><td>1<td>Pu Dong Airport<td>Hong Qiao Airport<td>22 RMB / 2.65 USD
<tr><td>2<td>Pu Dong Airport<td>Shanghai Exihition Center (Near Ritz Carlton or People's Square)<td>19 RMB 
  / 2.28 USD<tr><td>3<td>Pu Dong Airport<td>Zun Yi Road<td>20 RMB / 2.40 USD<tr><td>4<td>Pu Dong Airport<td>East Jiang Wan Rd.<td>18 RMB 
/ 2.16 USD<tr><td>5<td>Pu Dong Airport<td>Shanghai Railway Station<td>18 RMB / 
  2.16 USD</table>

Source: <a href="http://campus.etang.com/html/academic/usa/leave/leave002.htm">etang.com</a>

The service time is 6:00~19:00 for downtown or 8:00~21:00 for Pu Dong Airport. For more information, you can call +86-21-38484500.

Hope this is useful for you if you travel to Shanghai.

<b>See also:</b>
<ul><li><a href="http://www.wangjianshuo.com/personal/places/pudongairport/Bus.htm">Photos</a> of the Airport bus
<li>Pudong airport site (<a href="http://www.wangjianshuo.com/personal/places/pudongairport/">PVGSITE</a>)</ul>

<font color=red><b>Updated:</font> Questions and Answers</b>

Felicia from Singapore asked
<blockquote>What is operation hours & days that  the bus from Pudong Airport to Shanghai Exhibition Center (Route #2) and vice versa operate?</blockquote>

A: It operates seven days a week. The first bus will leave Shanghai Exhition Center at 6:00 AM and returns at 8:00 AM from Pudong Airport. The last bus will leave Shanghai Exhibition center at 19:00 and returns from Pudong at 21:00

<blockquote>Is there fix timing for the buses daily eg departure every hour or half hour?</blockquote>

There is no fixed schedule for the bus. There is a fixed interval of <b>15 to 20 minutes</b>. For busy hours, it is scheduled with 15 minutes interval and the interval is 20 minutes normally. There is no definition of busy hours or normal hours. Mabe it depends on the mood of the operator. :-)

<blockquote>How do I go about getting bus tickets from Shanghai Exhibition Center to Pudong Airport?</blockquote>

You can buy tickets after get onboard the bus. You don't need a ticket to get onboard.

However, it is a little bit wired to find the bus stop. It is at the gate of Shanghai Exhibition Center on Nanjing Xi Rd. (or someone call it Nanjing Rd. West), opposite to Shanghai Center (Shanghai Center is also know for the Portman Riz-Carton Hotel inside). Please check your hotel receiption for detailed walking direction - there is no bus stop there though.

Tonight, I enjoyed the ice cream mooncakes from <a href="http://www.haagen-dazs.com/">Haagen-Dazs</a>. The Belgian chocolate flavor ice cream is really nice, as described on its <a href="http://www.haagen-dazs.com/segseg.do">web site</a>: "When the first spoonful melts in your mouth the moment is pure pleasure". 

Haagen-Dazs changed its products a lot to meet Chinese styles and festivals. It seems Haagen-Dazs did great job in penertrate into the <a href="http://thestar.com.my/kuali/recipes/moon4.html">mooncake market </a>of Shanghai. As I know, more than 10,000 joint-venture company employees received Haagen-Dazs mooncake certificates from efesco. This is also the third year I receive the Haagen-Dazs mooncake certificate. It must be one of the big deals of this 

It is not long since Haagen-Dazs appeared in Shanghai. I still remember I attended the opening ceremony of Haagen-Dazs in Shanghai Center six years ago. Now, it has opened about four stores in Shanghai (based on the stores I know). There are two Haagen-Dazs stores near the building I am <a href="http://www.wangjianshuo.com/personal/office/office.htm">working in</a>. One more store is under construction near my <a href="http://www.wangjianshuo.com/personal/meilong/index.htm">old apartmnt</a>. It also expanded its coverage to Beijing, Dalian, Guangzhou and Shenzhen, according to China Online's <a href="http://shop.store.yahoo.com/chinaonline/haaginchinsw.html">report</a>.

I have chatted with Bill Lum about another European company IKEA. I told him the store is very profitable in Shanghai and Beijing. 

<blockquote>"If there is a holiday or a promotion, there are sometimes as many as 10,000 people here, so many you can't move"

said Linda Shi, PR manager of IKEA Shanghai Store
Source: <a href="http://www.siamfuture.com/asiannews/asiannewstxt.asp?aid=765">siamfuture.com</a></blockquote>

It is very true. When the store opens in 1997, I have visited the store and only few people are there. The price in the store is considered very high. Now, every Saturday, there are so many people that "you cannot move". It is more like a supermarket of furnitures. 

They are going to the second store in Shanghai. With 35,000 square meters' store area, the new store will be the largest <a href="http://www.siamfuture.com/asiannews/asiannewstxt.asp?aid=765">IKEA </a>store in Asia. I was very supprised when Bill told me IKEA opened a store in San Francisco only one year before.

AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
TITLE: "Net Send" - Yet Another Type of Spam
STATUS: publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 1
ALLOW PINGS: 1
PRIMARY CATEGORY: Misc
CATEGORY: Misc

DATE: 09/23/2002 11:52:24 PM
-----
BODY:
SPAM IS A BIG HEADACHE FOR EVERY ONE ON THE NET.

<blockquote>"The activities of a small number of people are becoming a bigger problem for the Internet." via <a href="http://spam.abuse.net/">Fight Spam on the Internet</a></blockquote>

Recently, I found another form of spam, which is becoming more and more popular: NET SEND SPAM.

<b>What is NET SEND SPAM?</b>

It works this way: on any networked Windows computer, anyone can type the following command in command line window:

<blockquote>NET SEND 127.0.0.1 Hello</blockquote>

A message box will appear with the greeting word "Hello". Looks interesting, isn’t it? However, if you change the IP address to any other valid IP address and change Hello to your advertisement, the IP address owner will receive it. Moreover, a simple script can send the same message to thousands of IP addresses, or millions of, if the sender wants.

Still sounds interesting? Not at all! I don't want this to inspire anyone to do it. Never do it and never give it a try. I am the angry person here who is fighting back with this kind of spam - NET SEND SPAM.

<b>Net send spam under spotlight</b>

Now <a href="http://bestyan.vip.sina.com">Mr. Yan</a>, who owns <a href="http://bestyan.vip.sina.com">http://bestyan.vip.sina.com</a> has come on board of the Net Send Spammers. Every two or three days, this guy will send Windows message to my networked computer in my home. I may be working or reading news or composing a weblog - no matter what I am doing - chances are, a gray dialog box pops up and says:

<blockquote>Message from ZMZ to 211.161.107.*** on 2002-9-22 23:28:40

XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX http://bestyan.vip.sina.com XXXXXXXX

(Note: XXXXX is garbage characters that I cannot read on my computer)</blockquote>

It is annoying. It made me angry after I received six of such messages. I am almost mad after I receive more than ten of such messages. However, <a href="http://bestyan.vip.sina.com">Mr. Yan</a> seems to be a very good evangelist for his web site and does not care too much about my feelings. Later, I found he does not care about the feels of thousands of people. Keep reading to know how many people were affected...

Finally, after six invitations, I decided to visit this web site. 

<b>Visit the site</b>

It is a normal personal web page. The owner seems to be fond of poems. It lets me feel not THAT bad since it is not a commercial site.

This guy has a guestbook too. I checked it, and found there are some one already yelling there for the spam they received. Some people said:

<blockquote>Please stop prompting your site using this kind of spam message</blockquote>

Some said:

<blockquote>I am in Korea. I cannot read the characters you sent to me, but I can see the web site address. I am feeling angry since you sent this message to me</blockquote>

I also posted a long message (half screen long? Maybe) to describe the feeling when I receive this message and asked him not to do that. In my post, I also quoted <a href="http://www.alistapart.com/stories/writeliving/">Mark Bernstein</a>'s suggestions on bloggers:

<blockquote>Though you write with passion about things that matter greatly, always remember that it’s a big world, filled with people and stories. Don’t expect the world to stop and listen</blockquote>

<b>It worked</b>. Within five minutes, my post was deleted from the <a href="http://www.ynisp.com/free/bbs/index.asp?user=bestyan">guestbook</a>, along with other negative posts.

To be honest, I was really shocked when I see people doing this:<i>creating</i> a web site; <i>send messages </i>to thousands of people, millions of, maybe; <i>force</i> them to read; <i>DELETE</i> posts on his personal guestbook when he doesn't like.

I posted for the second time. This time, I added a note:

<blockquote>This message is deleted by our honored web owner, just as others who protests for his spam. I believe this message will be deleted again, just want those who saw this to know what happened.</blockquote>

What I expected is true. It is deleted within six hours.

Now, on <a href="http://www.ynisp.com/free/bbs/index.asp?user=bestyan">bestyan's guest book</a>, there are still 21 entries. I found the webmaster will delete anything negitive and leave those compliments. It is bad. Really bad.

I know I can stop any message like this by stop the Messenger service in my computer. But I'd like to be involved in further spam and see how it evolves and how bad it will be.

Would you suggest what we can do to fight against NET SEND SPAM? Write your comments here.

<b><font color=red>Update</font></b>
<ul><li><a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20021107_stop_net_send_spam.htm#000074">Stoping Net Send Spam</a> <i>Nov 7, 2002</i></li>
<li><a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20021120_flighting_back_for_net_send_spam.htm#000089">Fighting Back for NET SEND SPAM</a> <i>Nov 20, 2002</i></ul>

COMMENT:
AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
EMAIL: jianshuo@hotmail.com
IP: 207.46.71.13
URL: http://home.wangjianshuo.com
DATE: 11/06/2002 09:39:04 AM
Brian McWilliams, a nice reporter at Wired.com <a href="http://www.wired.com/news/storylist/0,2339,483,00.html">http://www.wired.com/news/storylist/0,2339,483,00.html</a> has written an article called "Spam Masquerades as Admin Alerts" one month ago on "Net Send Spam". Here is the URL:
<a href="http://www.wired.com/news/technology/0,1282,55795,00.html">http://www.wired.com/news/technology/0,1282,55795,00.html</a>

On the private email discussion with him, he pointed me to a URL that blocks Messenger Ad.
<a href="http://www.coffeecup.com/blocker/">http://www.coffeecup.com/blocker/</a>

I checked the web site and don't want to pay for the money.

My reason is that it is OK for most people to turn the Messenger Service off without much problem. Corperate users may have been protected by firewall so they won't receive this kind of Ad. Even if the firewall is not well configured, to add a filter in firewall is much cheaper that to buy everyone the software. Those who are most affected are home users. They connect to Internet via broadband, DSL, dial-up. For them, the administrator won't send any message like "network going down in 5 minutes", "building on fire" to them. They don't use printer this way too. So simply turn off the Messenger service.

On Windows 2000 or XP, Start -> Run -> "Services.msc" -> Messenger -> Disable.

Let me know if any of you have better solutions.
-----
COMMENT:
AUTHOR: Docslax
EMAIL: docslax@hotmail.com

DATE: 11/18/2002 01:35:49 AM
Not a better, per say, solution than Jian Shuo Wang's but another simple and free solution for home users to shut down the messenger service is to open a command prompt Start -> Run -> cmd.exe then type the following "net stop messenger" after which you'll see "messenger service is stopping".
To start it again for any reason open the command prompt again and type "net start messenger"
This is the equivalent of what Jian Shuo Wang's suggestion.
I have had alot of customers call me regarding the abuse of this feature hopefully MS fixes it soon, i like one of the ideas on this page, i think the messenger service should only have ever been for local network machines.

OK, so this takes a few mins and probably only works on XP but it's a start.

On your dial up connection you have an internet connections firewall tab.

click this and block access to port 18 on both tcp and udp.

This will allow local admin alerts but block internet alerts.

No need to buy additional software just use what microsoft supplies.

Regards

Rich

hey i found this out on a website you can thank me later 8) keep up the work, next time research the internet it can be easier 8P


Disabling the MS Messenger Service 


Windows XP
1. Click on the Start button and open the control panel.
2. Open the Performance and Maintenance control panel and go to Administrative Tools.
3. Now double-click on Services, then scroll to Messenger.
4. Double-click Messenger and click Stop to stop the service.
5. Change the startup type to Disable and click Apply at the bottom.
6. Click OK to exit window.


Windows 2000
1. Click on the Start button -> Settings -> Control Panel.
2. Double click on Administrative Tools.
3. Now double-click on Services, then scroll to Messenger.
4. Double-click Messenger and click Stop to stop the service.
5. Change the startup type to Disable and click Apply at the bottom.
6. Click OK to exit window.

 
Online Resources 
?a href="http://www.techtv.com/screensavers/answerstips/story/0,24330,3374542,00.html">http://www.techtv.com/screensavers/answerstips/story/0,24330,3374542,00.html</a>
?a href="http://www.mynetwatchman.com/kb/security/articles/popupspam/index.htm">http://www.mynetwatchman.com/kb/security/articles/popupspam/index.htm</a>

COMMENT:
AUTHOR: Kagehi
EMAIL: shadowfyr55@hotmail.com
IP: 66.185.228.2
URL: 
DATE: 02/26/2003 04:41:14 AM
Hmm. I am trying to track down how this works, but for a different reason. I personally think that disabling any service that 'might' be useful is sort of dumb, so here is my idea:

So far it seems that WinPopUp (the 9x version) and Net Send send a request to port 135 to find out what the correct port of the messenger is. You 'could' block this port for all users, except those IPs that you allow to use them, but a decent hacker could simply spam the most common ports it might use. Not to mention the possibility that 135 may be used to request port numbers for other services.

So here is my idea. Have a firewall like service that only allow reciept from IPs you tell it to allow. When it start up, have it poll the 135 port to get the actual port assigned to the messenger, then only pass messages on that port that come from a valid list. That way it can still be used for the original purpose by allowing 'your' network or some other authorized IP(s) to access it, but kills the spam.

Of course this is just a theory... I don't currently have NT/XP, nor do I have WinPopUp installed, so I am just nosing around as an intellectual excersise. ;) I do seriously wonder why no one else has even considered this sort of solution though.

AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
TITLE: Server Outage - My Home is Still Not a Perfect Datacenter
STATUS: publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 1
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: Website
CATEGORY: Website

DATE: 09/24/2002 11:39:58 PM
-----
BODY:
My dear readers,

You may not be access this web site from Sept 24 to Sept 26. This is due to the network outage at my home. The 48 hours is very hard for me. I made a somewhat stupid decision to <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20020913_network_infrustucture_in_my_home_in_shanghai.htm">host home.wangjianshuo.com at my home</a>. Actually, I have spent a lot of time checking the availability of the site, worrying about whether it is down, or is there any problem with the network. Hosting a web server in my house is really problematic and expensive. Here is why:

<ol><li>The electronic power. The need to keep the computer up and running every day and every minute. The power fee is no cheaper than the renting fee. To rent a pretty good server with ActivePerl, ASP and PHP support, it is only 380 RMB ($45) per year. That is about 1 RMB per day - I am paying more than 1 RMB for the power for my computer everyday - if you know my computer does not support hibernate. Thanks for <a href="http://companycn.com">CompanyCN.com</a> to provide this service for me. I am especially grateful for Miss Cao's great help during the setup.
<li>The network. The network provided by <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20020913_network_infrustucture_in_my_home_in_shanghai.htm">Great Wall Broadband</a> is good, it also has some problem. Recently, with the government strengthen the control over networks, it uses a new authentication method. It required end user to type in account name and password before accessing the network. Sometimes this will drop. If the network connection is dropped, there is no way to remotely resume the connection unless I am physically at the computer to do so. This is the reason why my site is down for 48 hours. It happened before, but this time, I am on <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20020922_packing_for_chengdu.htm">business trip to Chengdu</a> and cannot reset it.</ol>

P.S. This log is attached at the day of Sept 26, but it is written on Sept 24, since the computer may be down, but my writing won't. 
-----

AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
TITLE: Home.wangjianshuo.com Moved Out of my Home
STATUS: publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 1
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: Website
CATEGORY: Website

DATE: 09/25/2002 11:12:22 PM
-----
BODY:
This is the quickest decision I have ever made in my life - apply a hosting service for my blog <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com">home.wangjianshuo.com</a>.

<b>Why so urgent</b>

My site has been down for more than 24 hours. It is not acceptable for my site. Although it is a personal web site without any sponsor, I am still want to keep it as stable as possible. But 24 hours downtime has made the avaiablility of the site to be less than 99.7%. The commercial web site is targeting to 99.99% availability. I need to fix it, as soon as possible.

<b><a href="http://companycn.com">CompanyCN.com</a> is a good company</b>

Thanks for <a href="http://www.google.com/search?hl=en&ie=UTF-8&oe=UTF-8&q=%E8%99%9A%E6%8B%9F%E4%B8%BB%E6%9C%BA">Google</a> (Chinese site), I found CompanyCN.com in the first page of the result.

I'd like to especially thank Miss Cao who helped me a lot during the setup of the web site in 24 hours - from sending the cash to the company, to setting the domain name system, and to configuring the Perl with the required modules by Movable Type.

The price is pretty good, 380 RMB (45 USD) for one year's hosting for Perl, ASP and PHP. It is fine for me since it is still cheap after I <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20020924_server_outage_my_home_is_still_not_a_perfect_datacenter.htm">compared </a>the price between hosting it in ISP and in home.

<a href="http://netcraft.net">Netcraft.net</a> provides a very good <a href="http://uptime.netcraft.com/up/graph/?mode_u=off&mode_w=on&site=home.wangjianshuo.com">report</a> on the history hosting of this web site. From the report, you can monitor the hosting change:

<blockquote><b>Web Server and Hosting History for home.wangjianshuo.com</b>

OS  Server Last changed IP address Netblock Owner 
Windows 2000  Microsoft-IIS/5.0  26-Sep-2002  202.101.10.123   Shanghai Telecom Co. Qingpu Telecom Breaure   
Windows XP  Microsoft-IIS/5.1  19-Sep-2002  211.161.107.18   FOR GWBN SHANGHAI # 145 RESIDENTIAL COMMUNITY BROADBAND NETWORK USERS' BROADBAND ACCESS  </blockquote>
