AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
TITLE: Remove Xupiter.com Toolbar
STATUS: publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 1
ALLOW PINGS: 1
PRIMARY CATEGORY: Website
CATEGORY: Website

DATE: 02/08/2003 04:07:35 PM
-----
BODY:
Currently, I found my computer is infected by the annoying Xupiter.com toolbar. This is very annoying.

<b>The symptoms</b>

One day, I suddenly found whever I type a wrong URL, or when the server I want to visit does not respond, the URL is first changed to a strange format, something like
http://<font color=red>/?%20</font>msn.com, where <font color=red>/?%20</font> is inserted unexpectedly.

Meanwhile, the page of http://www.xupiter.com/search2error2.html is loaded. Sometimes another pop up window with Ad also appears.

This is really annoying!

<b>What is Xupiter.com?</b>

Thanks for <a href="http://www.pchell.com/support/xupiter.shtml">PC Hell</a> to give clear explaination of Xupiter.com as below:

<blockquote><b>What is Xupiter?</b>

Xupiter Toolbar browser plug-in tools that gets installed on your computer through a popup ad or driveby installation that installs many times without your permission. It can also be loaded as an Active X control in Internet Explorer.

Once installed on your computer, Xupiter proceeds to display pop-up and pop-under ads as you surf the net. It also adds the Xupiter Toolbar to your browser, adds links to your favorites, and changes your home page. Xupiter then proceeds to track your browsing habits and report back to a server.</blockquote>

It also listed the way to tell you if you have Xupiter on your computer.

<blockquote>Follow these instructions:
1) Click on Start, Run 
2) Type MSCONFIG and press Enter
3) Click on the STARTUP tab 
4) Look in the list for the following item

Xupiter Toolbar

5) If this item is in the list. You have Xupiter installed. Uncheck it to temporarily disable the toolbar.</blockquote>

Update: Now the Toolbar has been upgraded. In step 4, you may also see

<i>XupiterStartup2003</i>
<i>XTCfgLoader</i>

It will run C:\Program Files\Xupiter\upiterStartup2003.exe

If you find these, you have Xupiter installed.

<b>Remove it</b>

It does not work if you delete all files under C:\Program Files\Xupiter folder. On one hand, you cannot delete them directly since some of the files are in use, such as XTCfgLoader and XTUpdate.dll. On the other hand, deleting DLLs and Exe rudely are always dangerous and may lead to instable system.

The best way to is to turn it off by uncheck the check box before the two files in MSCONFIG and restart the computer. Xupiter is not removed but it is not annoying any more. If you want to manually remove it in a graceful way, check <a href="http://www.doxdesk.com/parasite/Xupiter.html">Doxdesk.com</a>'s page for more information.


P.S. Dang An ID 9904154 @ 021-62403626

AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
TITLE: Guangzhou Virus Outbreak - Pneumonia-type 
STATUS: publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 1
ALLOW PINGS: 1
PRIMARY CATEGORY: Misc
CATEGORY: Misc

According to friends in Guangzhou, unknown virus outbroke in Guangzhou in the previous week. It is widely believed that 200 people have been killed in Guangzhou alone till Feb 10 (two days ago) and more in other areas. The official report said there is only 5 died from the virus.

I was planning some visits to Guangzhou but I have to postpone the schedule.

There are some street phones of current Guangzhou.

Sorry Jian Shuo Wang, but it unfortunately has everything to do with the lack of political transparency and accountability.
The Guangdong provincial government, just like its Hong Kong counterpart, initially surpressed the scale of the outbreak hoping that the problem would soon blow over. That delay in informing the public, has turned what would have been a fairly easily contained outbreak into a virtual global pandemic. 
Sticking ones head in the sand might be a good idea when dealing with provincial politics, but it is not a good idea when trying to contain a potentially fatal communicable disease !

AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
TITLE: Golarger.com - NET SEND Spamer and Comment Spammer
STATUS: publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 1
ALLOW PINGS: 1
PRIMARY CATEGORY: Website
CATEGORY: Website

DATE: 02/27/2003 11:49:31 PM
-----
BODY:
When I opened my web server log today, I was surprised that many visitors are visiting my site via <a href="http://search.yahoo.com/bin/search?p=golarger">Yahoo!</a> or <a href="http://www.google.com/search?hl=en&ie=UTF-8&oe=UTF-8&q=golarger">Google</a> just to find out who is <i>golarger </i>or <i>golarger.com</i>. (Yes! I intensionally didn't hyperlink this URL since I don't want to contribute more traffic to this spammer's web site).

<b>Why are people interested in <i>golarger</i></b>

It is obvious the 221 hits for searching the exactly the same term <i>golarger</i> is not just by chance that people happen to think about this term together. When the sudden increase of a word in my web log, I know something special happened. This is the case of <i>golarger.com</i>.

The truth is, golarger.com sent out <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20021107_stop_net_send_spam.htm">Windows Messenger spam</a> to a lot of people, asking them to visit their web site.  I don't know how many yet.

According to <a href="http://www.workoffiction.net/">Work of Fiction</a>,  <b>Brad Nugget </b>received the popup box like this:
 
<center><blockquote>Message from GOLARGER on 2/15/2003 11:55:17 PM

www.golarger.com
www.golarger.com
www.golarger.com

We are the #1 MALE ORGAN ENLARGEMENT supplement on the web. We guarantee the success of our program or we will refund every penny. Come find out why more men AND WOMEN come to us than any other site.

Enlarge your member 1-3 inches in a matter of days!

www.golarger.com
www.golarger.com
www.golarger.com</blockquote></center>

<font color=gray>Brad, sorry that I cannot link to the orginal blog entry on the site since the archive link on this site does not work when I visited</font>

Someone even posted the Network Monitor result of the analysis <a href="http://www.freelists.org/archives/fanolug/02-2003/fullthread25.html">here</a>.

<b>Bad. Very bad!</b>

As always, I hate NET SEND SPAM of any kind. If you are interested, please see my previous blog entries (the pages enjoy the highest hit rate of my whole blog site) on NET SEND SPAM.

<ul><li><a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20020923_net_send_yet_another_type_of_spam.htm#000037">Net Send Spam - Yet Another Type of Spam</a> Sept 23, 2002
<li><a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20021107_stop_net_send_spam.htm#000074">Stoping Net Send Spam</a> Nov 7, 2002
<li><a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20021120_flighting_back_for_net_send_spam.htm#000089">Fighting Back for NET SEND SPAM</a> Nov 20, 2002
<li><a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20021221_let_people_advetisethere_is_nothing_wrong_with_it.htm#000122">Let People Advetise...There is Nothing Wrong with it</a>, Feb 13, 2003</ul>

<b>Why searching for golarger leads to my page?</b>

I was asking the same question then. This is another bad thing golarger did. Under my page of <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20021107_stop_net_send_spam.htm#000074">Stoping Net Send Spam</a>, <i>James </i>left a <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20021107_stop_net_send_spam.htm#comments246">comment</a> like this:

<blockquote>I mean, honestly... www.golarger.com should be the target of the next "Code Red"...

Posted by: James on February 14, 2003 02:25 AM </blockquote>

I did notice this entry but didn't pay much attention to this one. Now, the discussion on <i>golarger.com</i> is not popular on Internet, my page became one of the only 4 pages on Internet which contains golarge at the time this entry is created.

<b>James, the bloggerr comment spammer</b>

Again, beside being a "NET SEND SPAMMER", the lovely James has another title, blogger comment spammer - who sends their advertisement to blogger's comment system. I used the term from <a href="http://philringnalda.com/blog/2002/10/comment_spam_alert.php">this article.</a>

<b>The battle against Net Send Spam (NSS) just begins</b>

I thought everyone is hating spam, but Mr/Miss/Mrs Marketer told me the opposite thing. He commented in ths <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20020923_net_send_yet_another_type_of_spam.htm#comments132">comment entry</a> that

<blockquote>So, what do you do when you go to your mail-box outside of your home? Do you beat up the postman when he delivers a piece of junk mail or do you go to court because you received the latest sales flyer from Radio Shack or maybe you call ABC and NBC when your favorite movie is on TV and here comes a commercial. I think not! This whole Spam Issue makes me sick and you should be ashamed of yourself.

Let people advetise...there is nothing wrong with it...it is how you got your website on one of the top search engine pages....OH!, Maybe you forgot that!!!...</blockquote>

I also <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20021221_let_people_advetisethere_is_nothing_wrong_with_it.htm#000122">replied</a> the entry stating

<blockquote>However, net send advertisement directly popup on MY screen no matter what I am doing. It is just like someone jumping into my room and paint their advertisement on MY wall. I don't care if he/she do it on his wall or on his friends' wall - as long their friend is OK for that. But I am angry if I see these kind of popups....</blockquote>

<b>Hot debate on net send spam</b>

Many other people joined the debate on the topic of Net Send Spam under my page on <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20020923_net_send_yet_another_type_of_spam.htm#000037">Net Send Spam - Yet Another Type of Spam</a>. It is very interesting to see how people think of the same thing diffenetly.

<a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20020923_net_send_yet_another_type_of_spam.htm#comments145">Marketer</a>: 

<blockquote>I hope that I was able to maybe shed some light on this subject and enable you to look through the eyes of an Online Marketer who earns just over $3,000 per month Online. This is my small income to support six children of which three are being adopted by my beautiful wife and myself....</blockquote>

<a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20020923_net_send_yet_another_type_of_spam.htm#comments150">Const</a>:

<blockquote>In a word, i think such spamming in the cyber world is not ethical, although one might make a large amount of money from it....</blockquote>

<a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20020923_net_send_yet_another_type_of_spam.htm#comments152">Antimarketer</a>:

<blockquote>Yeah, now this ass marketer is telling us that if he has 3 adopted children and 3 of his own, he has the right to spam. so now if i go an adopt 6 kids, and have six of my own, i guess i can go and kill too, because i will be making a meanie 3000 dollars to feed my kids. what an asshole this guy is, and how stupid can he become ?? ...</blockquote>

<a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20020923_net_send_yet_another_type_of_spam.htm#comments158">Marketer</a>

<blockquote>I am asking this board to please use another term
other than SPAM when addressing this form of advertising. 

The word SPAM is incorrect, go and see for yourself. Spam relates ONLY to EMAIL...period!...</blockquote>

<a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20020923_net_send_yet_another_type_of_spam.htm#comments161">Reader</a>:

<blockquote>Well, first I have to say that I agree somewhat with marketer.

You pay for cable or satellite to see your movies on tv, then they send you their advertisements that they paid for.

It's pretty much the same with the internet. You paid for access, and someone else is paying to advertise where you can see it....</blockquote>

<a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20020923_net_send_yet_another_type_of_spam.htm#comments165">iX</a>:

<blockquote>Some boastingly thought this sort of SPAM should continue. I don't think so. There are certain types of Junk mail it is illegal to send, there are some forms of advertising on the Television that is illegal (subliminal), even though everyone has a TV and is capable to receive subliminal messages, it has been deemed illegal. Net Send messages take processing cycles and comsume memory and network bandwidth, which means I have fewer resources to perform more effective functions. Ditto to Web Popups and Popbacks. These things consume resources and are unsolicited advertising....</blockquote>

<a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20020923_net_send_yet_another_type_of_spam.htm#comments173">Graeme</a>:

<blockquote>In response to the pro spam ad post by Marketer, the patronising attitude of telling me to click "that little x" is not appreciated. Having to close the pop up is not the problem here, it's the intrusive nature of the advertising. What right does anyone have to force a box with their useless little message onto your screen. Not only is it annoying, but it can potentialy destroy someones work....</blockquote>

<a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20020923_net_send_yet_another_type_of_spam.htm#comments209">anon</a>:

<blockquote>Opt-in email advertising is not only ethical but also appropriate for small business owners in today's internet society.

I could go on for a while - but I think that my point has been made - IF YOU DON'T WANT TO RECEIVE THE MESSAGES - THEN TURN THE OPTION OFF....</blockquote>


<a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20020923_net_send_yet_another_type_of_spam.htm#comments228">SpamBlows</a>:

<blockquote>We don't like it. If you love spam so much give us all your ip address, and we'll spam the hell out of you, and we'll do it using a dynamic IP...how do you like them apples?...</blockquote>


<a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20020923_net_send_yet_another_type_of_spam.htm#comments243">Ryan</a>:

<blockquote>my friends and i have used net send for years at the university we attend. i was shocked to find out that people have began using such a useful tool as a means of mass advertising. i would like to point out to the readers out there that these people CLAIM to pay thousands, and if they are foolish enough they actually may, but in fact anyone with an extra 15 minutes can send these spam messages to every ip in the world for free....</blockquote>

<b>Want to be heard of what you think?</b>

AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
TITLE: My New Mobile - Alcatel OT715
STATUS: publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 1
ALLOW PINGS: 1
PRIMARY CATEGORY: My Life
CATEGORY: My Life

DATE: 03/03/2003 11:30:10 PM
-----
BODY:
After SIEMENS, MOTOROLA, NOKIA, SIEMENS, my fifth mobile is Alcatel OT715. I bought one today - I am very excited about it.

<b>Mobile phones</b>

I believe China, Korea and Japan are among the highest population of mobile holders. Take me as an example, I know persons around me all have mobile phones - my friends, my classmate, my colleagues, my friends' friends - all have mobiles. It seems mobile numbers are just like Social Security ID number - everyone has one. Don't get me wrong. I just talk about my life and people around me. Don't assume anyone in China has a mobile - after all, I am living in one of the most modern city. If I can, I should also be something like middle class.

<b>Alcatel OT715 is just designed for me</b>

I am not a fan of mobiles. I just need a mobile that just works. I do have some friends who know every details of almost every model from various manufactures. Obviously I am not that kind of person.

However, this model made me exited when I first saw the introduction from a magzine dedicated to mobiles.

More <a href="http://images.google.com/images?hl=zh-CN&ie=UTF-8&oe=UTF-8&q=ot715&sa=N&tab=wi&lr=">pictures</a> from Google

AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
TITLE: Taxi for families from Pudong Airport
STATUS: publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 1
ALLOW PINGS: 1
PRIMARY CATEGORY: Shanghai
CATEGORY: Shanghai

DATE: 03/09/2003 05:31:39 PM
-----
BODY:
<b>Question: How convinient it will be to hire a 7 to 10 passenger taxi from the airport.  Will it take long to wait for one?</b>

This question comes from Mr. Lim. 

Well. Most taxies in Pudong airport are the standard taxi - for 4 passengers at most. There is no larger taxi in general. I suggest you to take two taxies, or book a taxi in advance.

I am not sure if this is conveinient for you. You can call <b>+86-21-82222</b> for a <a href="http://www.wangjianshuo.com/personal/shanghai/taxi.htm">Dazhong taxi </a>(there is only 7 seat taxi at this line). Note: They may speak Chinese only.

Call <font color=red>+86-21-62758800 (Jin Jiang Taxi)</font> or <font color=red>+86-21-62580000 (Qiang Sheng Taxi)</font> for 10-person taxi reservation. It is the most convenient way to move around Shanghai for team activities and for families. The fee is exactly the same as traditional taxi plus 5 RMB (15 initial fee, including 3 km, 2 RMB per kilometer).

Daozhong, Jin Jiang and Qiang Sheng are the three best taxi companies in Shanghai.

AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
TITLE: Alcatel OT715
STATUS: publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 1
ALLOW PINGS: 1
PRIMARY CATEGORY: My Life
CATEGORY: My Life

DATE: 03/11/2003 07:21:17 PM
-----
BODY:
It has been 7 days since I <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030303_my_new_mobile_alcatel_ot715.htm#000168">bought</a> my new mobile <i>Alcatel OT715</i>. 

Resources on OT715 are very rare on the Internet. Wow. How can this happy? David has been <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030303_my_new_mobile_alcatel_ot715.htm#Comments285">wondering</a> about what Alcatel is. Well, Alcatel is not that famous as Motorola, Nokia or Siemens... It is a Franch company that runs very good business in China. I think it may also run good business in Russian since 1/2 of the content on Internet about Alcatel OT715 returned from Google are either in Chinese or in Ruassian.

I am curious to know how many people in the world are using the same mobile as me. But the number should not be large, which can be reflected from the results of Google search for <a href="http://www.google.com/search?hl=en&lr=&ie=UTF-8&oe=UTF-8&safe=off&q=alcatel+ot715&btnG=Google+Search">Alcatel OT715</a> - 6K entries at the time when this page is created. How about <a href="http://www.google.com/search?hl=en&lr=&ie=UTF-8&oe=UTF-8&safe=off&q=nokia+3650">Nokia 3650</a>? There are 161K results.

There is an <a href="http://www.alcatel.com/products/productsummary.jhtml?_DARGS=/common/opg/products/include/productbrief.jhtml_A&_DAV=/x/opgproduct/One_Touch_500.jhtml">official website</a> about this mobile - but the site is among the slowest company sites I have ever seen. I am very disspointed about the site since it only contains beautiful pictures but don't have the user manual and function description that I need.

After long time seeking, I decide to share some of my experience. I have to say I love the mobile although I don't like its web site. It is a pity for a good mobile without a good page -- I mean a good page that can be find easily in Google. 

<blockquote>BTW, at the time this page is created, my previous page on OT715 is at the 10th place in the returning result of Google for "<a href="http://www.google.com/search?hl=en&lr=&ie=UTF-8&oe=UTF-8&safe=off&q=alcatel+ot715">Alcatel OT715</a>"</blockquote>

<b>Background</b>

Alcatel OT715 is launched in Hong Kong on July 15, 2002. It is available first in China and Hong Kong market, European market follows. At the time it is launched, it costs about 2500 RMB. At the time I bought it, its price drops to 1850 RMB in Shanghai.

<b>Features</b>

Here are the key features as listed in Alcatel's <a href="http://www.alcatel.com/products/productsummary.jhtml?_DARGS=/common/opg/products/include/productbrief.jhtml_A&_DAV=/x/opgproduct/One_Touch_500.jhtml">offical web site</a> for OT715. My comments are added under each feature.

<b>Infrared interface & serial link</b>

Well. This is a very good feature. I use it to
<ul><li>put the pictures of my house and girl friend into the handset, and show it as standby screen.

<img alt="shanghai-fanfan-on.OT715.png" src="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/2003/03/11/shanghai-fanfan-on.OT715.png" width="96" height="104" border="0" /> <img alt="shanghai-fanfan.leaning-on.OT715.png" src="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/2003/03/11/shanghai-fanfan.leaning-on.OT715.png" width="96" height="104" border="0" />
 and <img src="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/2003/03/03/shanghai-vanke.waltz.garden.png">

This can be accomplished via Creation Studio that comes with the mobile. The Infrared port is very handy to get the image from my Acer TravelMate 360.
<li>Transfer contact information to and from other mobile and laptop with Infrared Interface. I always think the connection between computer and mobile are too complicated. But the transfer of contact information of Alcatel OT715 is an exception. Here are the simple steps:
<ul><li>On the handset, click Tools -> Infrared.
<i>The mobile will report "Infrared is activated". Meanwhile, a small icon indicating Infrared will appear at the taskbar.</i><li>Put the mobile phone near the Infrared port of a laptop computer.
<i>The computer and the mobile should connect with each other automatically. 
OT715 should show "The infrared has been connected successfully." and the laptop computer should show "Another computer is near by", then change to "Wireless link with Alcatel OT715 at 115220 bps" <img alt="computer-wireless.with.OT715.PNG" src="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/2003/03/11/computer-wireless.with.OT715.PNG" width="242" height="49" border="0" />.</i><li>Choose a contact person on OT715 and select Transfer from the menu.
<li>Answer "Yes" when the Infrared manager on laptop computer ask you whether you want to receive the document.
<li>The file will be saved on the laptop in the format of a VCard. (Typically it will appear on your desktop). You can open the VCard using notepad if you don't have any VCard Management software like Outlook. Here is the content of a VCard.
<blockquote>BEGIN:VCARD
VERSION:2.1
N;CHARSET=UTF-8:Jian Shuo Wang;
TEL;WORK:02163352266P6656
TEL;CELL:13916146826
TEL;HOME:XXXXXXXXX
END:VCARD</blockquote>
</ul>
<li>For the serial line, I don't think it is useful since the software IntelliSync always crashes on Windows XP that I cannot complete a sync with my Outlook.
</ul>

There should be more functions other than transfering VCard or Image. I will post for more functions after I discovered it.

<b>Built-in GSM/GPRS (class 10) modem</b>

What is this? I have to admit that I don't learn new things as quick as I do 10 years ago. I have no idea about the GSM/GPRS modem, let along the term of "class 10".

I noticed that when the mobile is connected with my laptop via Infrared Port, an additional modem called "Modem - Standard Modem over IR link (COM4)" appeared on my Windows XP laptop. I can create a Dial-Up connection using this modem, but whenever I dial, it will fail. The encouraging message is, when I dial-up using the connection, the mobile will dial out as I am using the dial-pad to dial and the mobile displays "Outgoing Call 8163" (8163 is the Internet access number in Shanghai). However, it prompted "Service not available" very soon.

I assume that it is because I don't subscribed the Digital Data service from my NSP (network service provider). I plan to apply for this function and have a try later.

<b>Vcard & Vcalendar exchange</b>

I have covered this in "Irared Interface" section before. Thank God that the standard of VCard is reached so it can communicate with other mobiles and other applications.

<b>PALM & Windows CE devices compatible</b>

Not sure what this item means. I happen to have a Palm PDA. Let me give it a try to see if there is any possible connection between the two devices.

<b>EMS release 4.0</b>

I was told that I can send music with the message to my friends. It can also attach some 32x32 icons like these: 
<img alt="cat.png" src="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/2003/03/11/cat.png" width="32" height="32" border="0" /> <img alt="squirrel.png" src="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/2003/03/11/squirrel.png" width="32" height="32" border="0" /> <img alt="lion.png" src="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/2003/03/11/lion.png" width="32" height="32" border="0" />

However, this does not help me a lot since I don't want to waste time to attach a piece of music before I am very sure the my friend also have EMS 4.0 functions. 

<b>Ring tones & animated icons messaging</b>

Here are some of the pictures shipped with the mobile.

<img alt="big_boss.png" src="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/2003/03/11/big_boss.png" width="96" height="56" border="0" /> <img alt="boat.png" src="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/2003/03/11/boat.png" width="96" height="56" border="0" />

<b>Download facilities</b>

I am not very sure about what the download facilities means. It may be only available when WAP service is available. I didn't pay for the WAP service yet. It seems that the download here refer to downloading from a computer instead of downloading from Internet.

<b>Interactive games</b>

The three games come with Alcatel OT715 LOOK interesting:
<ul><li>Killer Expo
<li>Run Run Run
<li>Botwar</ul>

But I have to say the games are too fancy to be put into this small screen -- although Alcatel OT715 has the largest screen of a mobile phone, it is still too small to play games. I don't play any of the games. Sorry for the hardworking programers who created them.

<b>Two-player network game</b>

I don't know how to use this feature yet. The users' manual are just like the help document of Microsoft products - professional, well formatted but does not help at all. My quesiton is, why a mobile phone designed for "the high-end market" has so many game feature? Do they really expect business man to play games? Or will they play a two-player network game with another business man?

<b>Multi-field directory</b>

Yeh! This is the killer feature of OT715. For each individual, there are fields like Name, Mobile phone, Work phone, Home phone, Email, Address, City, Fax. These features are so handy to store two or three numbers under a single contact. When I want to dial out, two or three options are shown and let me choose to dial to his/her mobile or phone at work or phone at home. This works great for me. When I was using SIEMENS 3508, I have to create two seperate entries: Mr. Lin (HOME) and Mr. Lin (MOBILE) for the same person. The nightmare is finally over.

<b>Scheduler, To Do list</b>

I may be a good feature but nothing is impossible before I can setup the IntelliSync work on my Windows XP. As I have stated, it always crashes when I try to sync.

<b>PC & Over the Air synchro (SyncML)</b>

This feature seems fantastic. But give me some time to make it work. I may ask the helpful hotline guy to find out the answer.

I read about SyncML Server from time to time on Internet. Can I setup my own SyncML Server on home.wangjianshuo.com? There are too many questions in my mind.

<b>High resolution display</b>

<img src=http://www.pconline.com.cn/market/sh/shoppingguide/shuma/10208/pic/11582399pic1.jpg>

Look at the mobile. It looks so nice!

<b>Up to 10 lines of text (100x150 pixels)</b>

This feature is self-explainary. I don't need a color-screen mobile which is exteremly popular nowaways. All I need is information, instead of colorful pictures. This design of OT715 just works for me.

<b>4 gray scale quality
EL film with blue backlight color</b>

Very nice features that makes the modem look cool. It is announced that this mobile is "Men Mobile". Exactly.

<b>Zoom function & landscape viewing</b>

Where is the Zoom function? I cannot find it anywhere on the mobile.

<b>WAP 1.2.1 (Openwave micro browser)</b>

I am afraid I will use GPRS instead of WAP. WAP is expensive!

<font color=red>Updated</font> <i>March 19, 2003</i>

After another 7 days of this entry, I found the WAP function of Alcatel OT715 very useful. I have subscribed to GPRS service and can browse all the WAP sites. Further more, I <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030319_blog_on_wap.htm#000181">added WAP function to this blog</a>. That means, I can check who left comment on my web site and the hit counter of the page in real time. If you also have a WAP-enabled mobile, just try to browse http://home.wangjianshuo.com/wap/. I do feel "Information At My Fingertips" now.

<b>SATK Class 3 Release 99</b>

What is the new term of SATK again? Even Google <a href="http://www.google.com/search?hl=en&lr=&ie=ISO-8859-1&safe=off&q=SATK+Class+3&btnG=Google+Search">cannot answer</a> this question. SATK Class 3 seems to be the place on Internet to mention this term. Will keep investigating this.

<font color=red>Updated</font> <i>March 19, 2003</i>

I see. It is SIM Application Tool Kit. I remember the service provider once asked me to change to another SIM card for free. It will add a new item under my main menu -- services. The application is burned into the SIM card and can be accessed by the mobile. 

<b>Location services enabled</b>

Does it mean the mobile can tell me where I am? The altitude and longtitude? If it is the case, it will be super cool. But I don't see any interface on the mobile yet.

<b>M-Services compatible</b>

I have to doubt the propose of this spec: why there are so many hard-to-understand terms in the spec? I have never heard of M-Services, do you?

With the help of <a href="http://www.threegmobile.net/gallery/alcatelot715/">this webpage</a>, I guess the M-Services are something like downloading service with OpenWav's WAP Browser. Does it mean I can download a wall paper via WAP and show it on my mobile? It seems good. I can put my pictures on my web site and download it using my phone.

<b>Key Benifit</b>

Xtra large display.
Personal assistant.
GPRS.
Networking games.
Photograph download.
PC Software Suite.
 
<b>Resources</b>

Nice sites about Alcatel OT715
<ul><li><a href="http://www.rg1.co.uk/alcatel-one-touch-715.php">Alcatel OT715</a> on Funfone.net
<li><a href="http://www.my-onetouch.com/worldwide/com/products/phones/ot715/functions/photo/">Photograph download</a> feature
<li><a href="http://www.threegmobile.net/gallery/alcatelot715/">http://www.threegmobile.net/gallery/alcatelot715/</a></ul>

<b>Fee of China Mobile </b>

Here is the fee of China Mobile Communication Corp. (a.k.a CMCC)

Monthly subscription fee: 50 RMB/month
Local call: 0.4 RMB/min
Long distance call: 0.4 RMB/min + 0.07 RMB/6 seconds = 1.1 RMB/min

Good way to save money:
Dial 17951 + Long distance number: 0.7 RMB/min


<b>Alcatel OT715 Specification</b>

<blockquote>
Dimensions : 116x43x20mm (L x W x H)
Weight : 88 g
Talk time : Up to 6h30 (Pmin, 50%DTX)
Standby time : Up to 250 h (Paging 5, static)
Dual band : E-GSM 900 / DCS 1800
Standards : GSM Phase 2 / Phase 2+
Speech codec : EFR / FR / HR
Patch antenna
Standard battery : Lithium Polymer
DriveKey?: 5 positions
Enhanced blue backlight
Speech Codec : EFR/FR/HR
SIM card : 1.8 / 3V SIM, 3V SIM, 3 / 5V SIM. Not compatible with 5V only SIM.
SATK : SIM Application ToolKit Class 3 Release 99
WAP : WAP 1.2.1</blockquote>

COMMENT:
AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
EMAIL: jianshuo@hotmail.com
IP: 210.22.110.227
URL: http://home.wangjianshuo.com
DATE: 03/12/2003 09:03:39 AM
David,

I am afraid the payment rule is China is, the sender of the SMS pays the money. It is not expensive - 0.1 RMB per message, but you need to find a working mobile to work.

There are many websites here that you can send SMS. For example, <a href="http://sms.sina.com.cn,">http://sms.sina.com.cn,</a> <a href="http://sms.163.net.">http://sms.163.net.</a> You can get more information if you can read Chinese from the sites. What you need is a mobile phone user name (the phone number) and password. - In China, the password is sent to your mobile upon request. The fee wil be charged to your mobile bill.

I am not 100% sure about whether your mobile should work in China or not. There are three bands of GSM in the world - GSM 900/1800/1900 MHz. Only a Tri-Band can work around the world. I am not sure about which band Canada is using.

TITLE: Fixing and Changing on Wangjianshuo.com
STATUS: publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 1
ALLOW PINGS: 1
PRIMARY CATEGORY: Website
CATEGORY: Website

DATE: 03/12/2003 11:53:54 PM
-----
BODY:
<b>Fixing</b>

The <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/bbs/YaBB.cgi?board=PVG">PVGBBS</a> has been out of order for about one month. Whenever I click on any of the post, it always report:

<blockquote>Untrapped Error:
./sources/display.pl does not return a value from E:\Customer\Wangjianshuo\...</blockquote>

This is an annoying error and I looked it up on Internet and didn't find any suggestions. Actually, the error message is too broad and does not help.

Finally, after I backup all the files into my local disk, I suddenly noticed that display.pl has the size of 0 byte. How can it happen? I downloaded another copy of YABB Gold 1 SP 1.0 and replaced the problematic display.pl - everything works like a charm. 

It turned out that during the change of web server, the staff from my ISP didn't migrate my site completely. There are some posts and files lost during the migration, but the affect is minor.

<b>Changing</b>

The homepage of <a href="http://wangjianshuo.com">wangjianshuo.com</a> is changed to the new style:

News from <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com">Wangjianshuo.com's blog</a> (this web site) appears on that static web site using VBScript. 

If you are also using MovableType, just create a new index template named "News Feeding VBScript" and let it create page named news.vbs. Use the code below as the content of the template, save it and rebuild, your blog newsfeed is ready.

Here is the source code of the VBScript generating the headlines:

<blockquote>&lt;script language=vbscript src=&quot;http://home.wangjianshuo.com/news.vbs&quot;&gt;&lt;/script&gt;&lt;

On Error Resume Next
Sub PrintNews()
strNewsHTML = &quot;&quot;
&lt;MTEntries lastn=&quot;7&quot;&gt;
strNewsHTML= strNewsHTML + &quot;&lt;a href=&lt;$MTEntryLink$&gt;#&lt;$MTEntryID pad=&quot;1&quot;$&gt;&gt;&lt;$MTEntryTitle$&gt;&lt;/a&gt; 
&lt;span class=posted&gt;&lt;$MTEntryDate format=&quot;%B %d&quot;$&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&quot;
&lt;/MTEntries&gt;

Document.Write strNewsHTML
End Sub

Call PrintNews</blockquote>

Adding the following line to the webpage (<a href="http://www.wangjianshuo.com/index.htm">http://www.wangjianshuo.com/index.htm</a>) and the headline is displayed automatically.

<blockquote>&lt;script language=vbscript src=&quot;http://home.wangjianshuo.com/news.vbs&quot;&gt;&lt;/script&gt;</blockquote>

This is the redesigned homepage.

<a href="http://www.wangjianshuo.com"><img alt="computer-wangjianshuo.com.2003.3.12-change.PNG" src="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/2003/03/12/computer-wangjianshuo.com.2003.3.12-change.PNG" width="786" height="500" border="0" /></a>

You can provide me some feedbacks regarding the redesign using the comment function with this blog.

AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
TITLE: Best of Febuary 2003 Blog
STATUS: publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 1
ALLOW PINGS: 1
PRIMARY CATEGORY: Website
CATEGORY: Website

DATE: 03/13/2003 09:21:58 PM

BODY:
20:58

This article summarizes my blog entries of Febuary 2003, so you can find information you want  more easily.

Febuary is the shortest month of the year. There is 28 days in 2003, among which, 7~9 days are Chinese Spring Festival. There is only 10 blog entries in this month

In this month, there is a piece of breaking news - <b>golarger</b> spam. I <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030227_golargercom_net_send_spamer_and_comment_spammer.htm#000165">described</a> what is golarger spam and <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030228_fight_back_for_golarger_spam.htm#000166">quoted</a> <b>Simo</b>'s complain email to fight back this spam. It is interesting that a lot of people find my page in the #1 position in Google result for golarger. So they think I am the one who send out spam to them. They complained and posted <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030227_golargercom_net_send_spamer_and_comment_spammer.htm#Comments282">here</a> and <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030228_fight_back_for_golarger_spam.htm#Comments317">there</a>.   

Like golarger, Xupiter is another kind of annoying spam. I described about this and linked to articles to remove it in <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030208_remove_xupitercom_toolbar.htm#000159">this entry</a>.

Althought it is the holiday season, the people in Guangzhou and surrounding areas are not that lucky. <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030212_guangzhou_virus_outbreak_pneumoniatype_.htm#000160">Pneumonia-type virus outbreak in Guangzhou</a>. It has been said the situation <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030216_eyes_on_guangzhou.htm#000162">became worse</a> several days later.

There is something interesting too. More <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030205_thanks_for_linking_my_site.htm#000157">website</a> are linking to me; I found a good way to <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030206_shanghai_pudong_airport_to_suzhou.htm#000158">go from Pudong Airport to Suzhou</a>. I <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030223_update_about_these_weeks.htm#000163">went to Beijing</a> for about four days. It was sunny there.

That's all for my Febuary in 2003. Check <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/2003_02.htm">here</a> for more details.

AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
TITLE: Mobiles in China - My Personal Perspective
STATUS: publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 1
ALLOW PINGS: 1
PRIMARY CATEGORY: Shanghai
CATEGORY: Shanghai

DATE: 03/15/2003 12:30:48 PM
-----
BODY:
<b>Huge Mobile Subscribers Amount</b>

According to the latest report from the Ministry of Information Industry on Dec 17, 2002, by the end of Nov 2002, the number of mobile subscribers has reached <b>200.3</b> million. 

<blockquote>Mobile phone subscriber # <b>200.31</b> million
Fixed-line telephone subscriber # <b>212.68</b> million
Telephone total subscribers # <b>412.99</b> million
Internet users # <b>48.29</b> million

# of telephone subscribers by the end of Nov 2003, according to Ministry of Information Industry, China
</blockquote>

From the begining of 2002, there are about 5 million new mobile subscribers. With this trend going on, the number of mobile subscribers will exceed the one of fixed-line telephone very soon. The number of 200 million subscribers means every 100 persons in China have 14.95 mobiles. This number in big cities like in Shanghai and Beijing is much higher.

<b>My personal perspective</b>

From my personal perspective, there is vivid persons and lives behind these abstract numbers. I bought my mobile five years ago when I was still a student. My girlfriend bought hers 6 years ago. I don't have any friend who don't have a mobile in Shanghail now - my estimation is, any well-educated young people in Shanghai have a mobile.

What surprises me a lot is, even the workers decarating my house have their mobiles - the painters, the decorators, the mason, the electricity, and the carpenter. They dressed poorly - they don't bath for weeks, but they have mobiles. It is amazing!

I do have one friend in Shanghai who only have a pager - a 70-year-old famous professor. Beside him, I don't know anyone without a mobile phone.

Mayor of WebmasterWorld <a href="http://www.webmasterworld.com/forum32/322.htm">described</a> his vision for China when he was here in 70's. 

<blockquote>Having spent some time in PRC in the late '70's, my vision of the Peoples Republic is still one where there is little electric power or communication infrastructure, except to a limited amount in major cities. It's still a vision of technology mired in the 1940's. </blockquote>

It is quite true that in late 70's, there is almost on communication infrustructure. But now, it has changed greatly.

<b>Impression of my friends in US</b>

Some friends of mine came to Shanghai from Seattle. They are talking about the mobile and communication infrustcture in China excitedly - "Can you imagine it? My mobile phone still gets signals in the mountains that are hours' car ride from Chengdu!!" I happent o have the <a href="http://www.wangjianshuo.com/personal/places/daocheng/maphis/index.htm">pictures</a> of the mountains he described.

When I was travelling in Seattle, I found it insteresting that a lot of people don't have mobiles. People explained this to me: in the north Americian, the telephone infrusturct has been built very well and you can easily find a telephone anywhere. But in China, to find a telephone on the street is not as easy. So there is a huge demand to get a mobile. 

<b>Fee of China Mobile</b> 

Here is the fee of China Mobile Communication Corp. (a.k.a CMCC)

Monthly subscription fee: 50 RMB/month
Local call: 0.4 RMB/min
Long distance call: 0.4 RMB/min + 0.07 RMB/6 seconds = 1.1 RMB/min
Answer phone: 0.4 RMB/min

Good way to save money:
Dial 17951 + Long distance number: 0.7 RMB/min

(note: 1 USD = 8.3 RMB)

For me, I use my mobile frequently. For local calls and long distance calls. I get a bill of around 300 RMB every month.

<b>Mobile phones</b>

Mobile phones in China is cheap. For some old-fasioned mobiles, it only costs about 300+ RMB (40 USD?) to get a mobile. It is different than in U.S. Mobile phone and the SIM card are sold seperately. You can buy any mobile you like and choose the NSP (network service provider). Any two can macth. There is a discount to buy a mobile with a SIM card though.

Big mobile phone companies are fighting for bigger market share aggressively. It is clear that Nokia is taking the leading position and Motorola follows. My new mobile is <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030311_alcatel_ot715.htm#000172">Alcatel OT715</a>.

<b>Network Service Providers</b>

There are three large NSPs in China
<ul><li>China Mobile - the largest. I am using China Mobile.
<li>China Telecome
<li>China Unicom - this is the provider of my girl-friend's</ul>

Actually, I don't see much difference between the service they provide. 

Besides the subscription fee based model, they also have other options, like Prepaid Card.

<b>Pre-paid Card</b>

All the providers offer their pre-paid card. Users of these card don't have to pay for the monthly subscription fee, don't have to pay the bill. They just buy a card (with a SIM card and certain amount of fee). There is a mobile phone related to this SIM card. Insert the SIM card into any mobile and you gain instant access to the mobile network. 

Before the prepaid amount of money is used out, you can buy "value card", which is about 50, 100, 200 RMB. Unveil the card number and password, call the provider's number, key in the card number and password, you gain additional communication time. It is easy. The charge of this card per minute is a little bit higher than the monthly subscription model. 

I have a lot of phone calls so I choosed the subscription based. My girl friend don't use her mobile as frequently, so she bought the prepaid card.

<b>Pre-paid card in action</b>

Here is an example of the Shenzhouxing pre-paid card from China Mobile (CMCC).

<img alt="shanghai-shenzhouxing-card.jpg" src="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/2003/03/15/shanghai-shenzhouxing-card.jpg" width="230" height="145" border="0" />
<i>Shenzhouxing card. You can see the SIM card on the left.</i>

Local: 0.6 RMB/min
Domestic long distance: 0.6 RMB/min + 0.07 RMB/6sec
Answer call: 0.6 RMB/min

You can compare the rate with subscription-based rate listed before. Please note: both calling out and answering call are charged, at the same rate.

<b>Signal coverage</b>

Here is the China Mobile Communication Corp. (CMCC) <a href="http://telecom.chinabyte.com/20030310/1656100.shtml">report</a> on signal coverage from ChinaByte on March 10, 2003

<blockquote>In the 36 major cities, avg. coverage = 99.86%
Country-wide highway coverage = 96%</blockquote>

In big cities like Shanghai, the coverage is a big challenge. There are two many tall buildings that weakens the signal. Now, most places are covered, such as in metro tunnel, in most elevators.

<b>Related</b>

<ul><li><a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030316_micropayment_with_mobile_sms_in_china.htm#000177">Micropayment with Mobile SMS in China</a></ul>

AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
TITLE: Micropayment with Mobile SMS in China
STATUS: publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 1
ALLOW PINGS: 1
PRIMARY CATEGORY: Shanghai
CATEGORY: Shanghai

DATE: 03/16/2003 08:50:05 AM
-----
BODY:
<b>Related entries</b>: <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030315_mobiles_in_china_my_personal_perspective.htm#000178">Mobiles in China - My Personal Perspective</a>

I read about <a href="http://www.webmasterworld.com/forum32/322.htm">discussion</a> on webmasterworld.com. Let's try to describe the society I am in. I live in Shanghai, China.

<b>SMS is hot; SMS is part of people's life in China</b>

I couldn't image there is anything that affected people's life more than Internet two years ago. Now I realized SMS is competing with Internet to change people's life.

In China, there is only 48.29 million Internet users by end of Nov, 2002 (don't get me wrong, this number is huge already), but there are 200.3 million mobile users. 

I have a friend who spend about 100 RMB every month for SMS. It is only 0.1 RMB per SMS, which means 1000 SMS every month. Young generation (16-20 years old) use SMS more frequently. As I described in this article, <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030315_mobiles_in_china_my_personal_perspective.htm#000178">Mobiles in China - My Personal Perspective</a>, some people just buy a mobile phone and a pre-paid card. They only use the SMS functions as a good way to save money. They don't use the mobile phone to call.

<b>SMS + TV? SMS + Radio? SMS + newspaper? SMS + ....</b>

SMS is no longer a method for peer-to-peer communication. Some TV programs uses SMS as a feedback channel from the audience. They will put a survey on TV and they can get instant feedbacks. For example, in some competitions, SMS sent by audience will be a factor to choose the final winner. It is the same for the combination of SMS + Radio or newspaper.

<b>SMS applications</b>

More and more companies in Shanghai are using SMS as the information platform. There is a company called Guangxi (or Relation in English). You can send a SMS message to their service number 885074 containing any place name, and they will return the result to you via SMS. It is very handy.

CMCC (China Mobile) allows you to send JFCX to 1861 to query your credit in CMCC. Even the government is using SMS as a quick way to validate the invoice. This way, people cannot make fake invoices.

<b>SMS + Internet</b>

The reason why SMS can generate revenue is, the provider can charge more than the standard 0.1 RMB/message. In <a href="http://sms.sina.com.cn">http://sms.sina.com.cn</a>, for example, people can download rings, pictures. Sina.com will charge 1.0 RMB/message for most of the download. The fee will appear in the monthly bill of mobile fee of the users. Then communication companies like CMCC will share the revenue with Sina.

For companies like 5460.net, a classmate finder service, information is no longer free. If you want to find a long lost classmate, you can enter his/her name, and the site will list very limited information about the person you are looking for. If you want to get more like his email, mobilephone, ..., you need to enter your mobile phone number. The site will send it to you. The trick is, if the site display is on the web site, it is free. But if they send it to you, they can charge you 1 RMB. That is the different. Although it is very small amount of expense for you, the thousands of subscribers do add up to big money.

Hereby, I'd like to announce that I am married with <a href="http://www.wangjianshuo.com/personal/fanfan/fanfaninnewhouse/">Wen Feng Fan</a> (Wendy Fan) today. After getting know each other for 6.5 years, we finally setup the family. I'd like to share the good news with you.

<a href="http://www.wangjianshuo.com/personal/fanfan/fanfaninnewhouse/"><img alt="shanghai-fanfan-in.white.red.lean.jpg" src="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/2003/03/17/shanghai-fanfan-in.white.red.lean.jpg" width="100" height="75" border="0" /></a> <a href=http://www.wangjianshuo.com/personal/fanfan/fanfaninnewhouse/><img alt="shanghai-fanfan-in.white.red.hands.on.head.jpg" src="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/2003/03/17/shanghai-fanfan-in.white.red.hands.on.head.jpg" width="100" height="75" border="0" /></a> <a href="http://www.wangjianshuo.com/personal/fanfan/fanfaninnewhouse/"><img alt="shanghai-fanfan-white.red.wet.hair.jpg" src="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/2003/03/17/shanghai-fanfan-white.red.wet.hair.jpg" width="100" height="75" border="0" /></a>

We will hold the wedding ceremony at the begining of May. Here are the details:

Date: <b>May 6, 2003</b>
Venue: <b>3th Floor, Penoy Plaza, Luoyang, Henan, China</b>

We invite all our friends, families to attend our ceremony. Please give us your confirmation using the comment system below. Thanks.

<b>About Wendy</b>

Wendy is one year younger than me but we entered the same university at the same year. Both of us took the China Southern Airlines flight from Zhengzhou to Shanghai in the year 1995. (The air tickets were gifts from the airline since I took the first place of all new students of Henan province while she was in the third place).

She studied Computer Science while I majored in Automation. We first saw each other in end of Sept, 1996. After I graduated, I entered Microsoft and she continues to work on her master's degree. Two and half years later, very interestingly, she also choosed Microsoft although she got offers from many companies including IBM and Intel.

We have been planning the wedding for some time and we are so happy to finally make it real. Congratulations to me and my wife, Fanfan.

AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
TITLE: Difference Between Quanqiutong and Shenzhouxing
STATUS: publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 1
ALLOW PINGS: 1
PRIMARY CATEGORY: Shanghai
CATEGORY: Shanghai

DATE: 03/19/2003 11:07:37 PM
-----
BODY:
John <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030315_mobiles_in_china_my_personal_perspective.htm#comments335">asked</a> what is the difference between Quanqiutong and Shenzhouxing SIM card after my blog entry <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030315_mobiles_in_china_my_personal_perspective.htm">Mobiles in China - My Personal Perspective</a>. I believe it is a good topic to initiate a new article on this topic.

<b>Quanqiutong and Shenzhouxing in Chinese</b>

For people who don't speak Chinese, these two words are so strange that are even hardly to read. Before I dive into the technical difference part, let me explain the terms.

Quanqiutong is actually three characters (words) in Chinese:

<i>Quan Qiu Tong</i>

Let me try to explain the meaning although it is always not easy to directly translate Chinese.

<i>Quan</i> means <i>all</i>, <i>entire</i>
<i>Qiu</i> means <i>globe</i>, <i>the earth</i>
<i>Tong</i> means <i>connected</i>,<i>pass</i>

So combined together, it means "You can get connected throughout the whole world".

For Shenzhouxing, which can also be spelled as "<i>Shen Zhou Xing</i>"

<i>Shen</i> means <i>magic</i>,<i>grand</i>
<i>Zhou</i> means <i>state</i>,<i>country</i>
<i>Xing</i> means <i>travel</i>

<i>Shen Zhou</i> means <i>China</i> in Chinese language

So Shenzhouxing can be translated "Travel across China"

<b>Difference between Quanqiutong and Shenzhouxing</b>

These two SIM cards are all issued by China Mobile Communication Corp. (CMCC). Quanqiutong is subscription based card and Shenzhouxing is prepaid card. 

I didn't noticed it yet before I wrote this article - the names themselves described the difference between the two SIM card. 

For Quanqiutong (You can get connected throughout the whole world), it can be used in more than 50 counties with the roaming services. It has more functions than Shenzhouxing, like WAP, SMS Broadcast, IP Phone, Voice message, Data communication, Fax, Call transfer.... It provide the basic functions as most mobile providers. This is the majority of all CMCC users.

For Shenzhouxing, however, it can only be used in China as name implies: "Travel across China"

<b>Difference in payment methods</b>

The key difference does not lie in coverage. Quanqiutong takes the billing approach like fixed telephone - call first and pay at the end the month. So the application is relatively complicated since you need to provide your national ID card (or passport) and fill in the application form in the service centers of CMCC.

For Shenzhouxing, it takes the pay first then call approach. You can control your mobile fee by only deposit certain amount of money. Since it is prepaid card, anyone can buy any card freely from any dealer. There is no monthly subscription fee. What you need to do is to buy "value card" from time to time and enter the card ID and the password with the card via the service number 13800138000. 

<b>Prepaid or not prepaid, it is a question</b>

Prepaid card <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030315_mobiles_in_china_my_personal_perspective.htm#000178">charges</a> 0.6 RMB per minute for local calls at the time when this article is written. Quanqiutong charges 0.4 RMB per minute + 50 RMB monthly subscription fee. By simple calculation, you know that if dial local calls for 250 minutes in one month, the both cards charge you the same amount of money - 150 RMB. If you spend more than 250 minutes, Quanqiutong is more economic for you, otherwise, you'd better choose Shenzhouxing.

Let me know if you have more questions. BTW, I am using Quanqiutong SIM card.

<b><font color=red>Update</font></b> <i>March 26, 2003</i>

Jim reminded me that besides the two card mentioned before, China Mobile also provide two more prepaid cards: GoTone E-Tone Card and GoTone E-Da Card.

<img src=http://www.shmc.com.cn/English/images/001.jpg>
Logo of GoTone (Quanqiutong in Chinese)

It is the standard contract based (subscribe based) service, as refered in Quanqiutong in this article.

<a href="http://www.shmc.com.cn/English/fivegreat/shenzhou.htm"><img src=http://www.shmc.com.cn/English/images/04.jpg></a>
Logo of Shenzhouxing

This is the Shenzhouxing card. 0.15 RMB per SMS sent to CMCC mobiles or 0.20 RMB if sent to China Unicom mobiles.

<a href="http://www.shmc.com.cn/English/fivegreat/35_Etong.htm"><img src=http://www.shmc.com.cn/English/images/031.jpg></a>
Logo of GoTone E-Tone card

Prepaid card. 0.10 RMB per SMS for CMCC mobiles and 0.15 RMB if the message is sent to Unicom mobile from CMCC mobile. It is a local card only available in Shanghai - the card can be used outside Shanghai, but the recharge card and the SIM card is only available in Shanghai market.

<a href="http://www.shmc.com.cn/English/fivegreat/Gotone.htm"><img src=http://www.shmc.com.cn/English/images/02.jpg></a>
Logo of GoTone E-Da card

Enjoys the same charge standard as Quanqiutong (GoTone) - I have never seen it.

Quit confusing, isn't it?

Karp, as I know, the price for a Shenzhouxing Pre-Paid SIM card is 100 RMB. There is not communication fee included in the SIM card. You have to buy the value card which has: 50, 100, 300 and 500 RMB.

For the value card, it is easy to buy from any where - any small store or newspaper reseller should be reseller of the value card.

To buy SIM card, however, is not as easy. Any mobile store should have SIM card available. There are many stores around the city.

It should be fine for you, as non-English speaker to survive in Shanghai. I guess you can get the card without big problem. Although not everyone in Shanghai speak English, you can always find someone to help you interperret for you.

AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
TITLE: My Blog on My Mobile Via WAP
STATUS: publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 1
ALLOW PINGS: 1
PRIMARY CATEGORY: Website
CATEGORY: Website

DATE: 03/20/2003 11:21:46 PM
-----
BODY:
These days, I have setup the WAP site for <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com">Wangjianshuo's Blog</a>. I can get the latest comments on my web site and the total hit count from my <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030311_alcatel_ot715.htm#000172">mobile</a>. I'd like to share the source code and steps with all blog users - especially for MovableType owners since you can convert your web site to WAP site with the code I provide.

<b>How to access the WAP site</b>

If you have a <a href="http://www.google.com/search?hl=en&lr=&ie=UTF-8&oe=UTF-8&q=wap+enabled+mobile">WAP-enabled mobile</a>, please visit the following web site:

<blockquote><a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/wap/">http://home.wangjianshuo.com/wap/</a></blockquote> 

Here is the two images (left is the home page displaying all the comments and the right picture shows the hit counter)

<img alt="picture-ot715.wap-index.PNG" src="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/2003/03/20/picture-ot715.wap-index.PNG" width="222" height="175" border="0" /> <img alt="picture-ot715.wap-hits.PNG" src="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/2003/03/20/picture-ot715.wap-hits.PNG" border="0" />

The above are the simulated OT301 screen using UP.Simulator. I hope I can give you a picture of the page on my <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030311_alcatel_ot715.htm">Alcatel OT715</a> one day.

Note: If you click the link above in Internet Explorer, you will not see the page. Instead, you are prompted to download the page, since it returns "text/vnd.wap.wml" as content type which cannot be proccessed by Internet Explorer.

<b>The WAP page - WML file</b>

If you save the page to your local disk and open it in notepad, you will see the following codes:

<blockquote>&lt;?xml version="1.0"?&gt;
&lt;!DOCTYPE wml PUBLIC "-//WAPFORUM//DTD WML 1.1//EN" "http://www.wapforum.org/DTD/wml_1.1.xml"&gt;
&lt;wml&gt;
&lt;card id="index" title="Wangjianshuo's blog"&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="index.asp?id=353"&gt;Jian Shuo Wang&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="index.asp?id=352"&gt;p1gs1ck&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="index.asp?id=351"&gt;KLN&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;* &lt;a href="hits.cgi"&gt;Hits&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;/card&gt;
&lt;/wml&gt;</blockquote>

After you click the *Hits link, you get the following WML code:

<blockquote>&lt;?xml version="1.0"?&gt;
&lt;!DOCTYPE wml PUBLIC "-//WAPFORUM//DTD WML 1.1//EN" "http://www.wapforum.org/DTD/wml_1.1.xml"&gt;
&lt;wml&gt;
  &lt;head&gt;
    &lt;meta forua="true" http-equiv="Cache-Control" content="max-age=0"/&gt;
  &lt;/head&gt;
&lt;card id="hit" title="Page Hit"&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Page hits: 127502&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;[&lt;a href="index.asp"&gt;Back&lt;/a&gt;]&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;/card&gt;
&lt;/wml&gt;</blockquote>

<b>Code behind the sceen</b>

I used an ASP file to do the job. You can easily convert it to Perl or PHP code. If you are using MovableType, follow the steps below to create a WAP index template.

1. Open MovableType console and open the blog you are editing.
2. Click "Templates" on the left navigation bar.
3. Click "Click new index template" in the Index Template section.
4. Enter "WAP Index" in Name field and "WAP/Index.asp" in the Output file field.
5. Use the code below in the Template body field.
6. Save the template and rebuild. You will have the WAP page at WAP/index.asp.

<blockquote>&lt;% 
   '
   ' Copyright 2003 Jian Shuo Wang
   ' URL: http://wangjianshuo.com
   ' Author: Jian Shuo Wang
   ' Created: March 18, 2003
   ' Description:
   '   This page displays the latest comments
   '   on any mobile phone supporting WAP.
   ' 
%&gt;

&lt;% 
   Response.ContentType="text/vnd.wap.wml" 
   If Request("ID") = "" Then
      Response.Expires = -1 
   End If
%&gt;

&lt;% 
   '
   ' The standard header every card need
   '
%&gt;

&lt;?xml version="1.0"?&gt;
&lt;!DOCTYPE wml PUBLIC "-//WAPFORUM//DTD WML 1.1//EN" "http://www.wapforum.org/DTD/wml_1.1.xml"&gt;
&lt;wml&gt;
&lt;%

   Select Case Request("ID") 

   ' --------------------------------
   '  Comment content
   ' --------------------------------
%&gt;

&lt;MTComments lastn="5"&gt;
&lt;%
	Case "&lt;$MTCommentID$&gt;":
%&gt;
&lt;card id="index" title="&lt;$MTCommentAuthor$&gt;"&gt;
&lt;$MTCommentBody$&gt;
&lt;p&gt;- by &lt;$MTCommentEmail$&gt; at &lt;$MTCommentDate$&gt; from &lt;$MTCommentIP$&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;[&lt;a href="?"&gt;Back&lt;/a&gt;]&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;/card&gt;
&lt;/MTComments&gt;

&lt;%
	Case "":

   ' --------------------------------
   '  Homepage - Comment Index
   ' --------------------------------
%&gt;

&lt;card id="index" title="&lt;$MTBlogName$&gt;"&gt;
&lt;MTComments lastn="10"&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="index.asp?id=&lt;$MTCommentID$&gt;"&gt;&lt;$MTCommentAuthor$&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;/MTComments&gt;
&lt;p&gt;* &lt;a href="hits.cgi"&gt;Hits&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;/card&gt;

&lt;%
	Case Else:
%&gt;
&lt;card id="index" title="Wangjianshuo"&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Something wrong with the page&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="?"&gt;Back&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;/card&gt;
&lt;%
   End Select
%&gt;
&lt;/wml&gt;</blockquote>

<b>Comments on the code</b>

1. <i>Response.ContentType="text/vnd.wap.wml"</i> must be included since it let the WAP browser understand it is a WML content since it cannot be judged from the .ASP extension.
2. It may need some modification before it can work on your site.

TITLE: Physical Location of GOLarger.com
STATUS: publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 1
ALLOW PINGS: 1
PRIMARY CATEGORY: Website
CATEGORY: Website

DATE: 03/21/2003 11:11:19 PM
-----
BODY:
yolei81 <a href=http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030228_fight_back_for_golarger_spam.htm#comments371>posted</a> the WHOIS data for golarger.com - which has been under our investigation for a <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030227_golargercom_net_send_spamer_and_comment_spammer.htm">long</a> <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030228_fight_back_for_golarger_spam.htm">time</a>.

According to the WHOIS database, the location GOLarger.com's owner is:

<blockquote>Organization:
Jason Spencer
Bob Lerman
45 Henry St
Brooklyn, NY 11201
US
Phone: 718-654-7898
Email: b_lerman2002@yahoo.com</blockquote>

Here is the maps about this location on MapPoint.msn.com.

<img alt="newyork-henry.father.brooklyn.map-mappoint.gif" src="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/2003/03/21/newyork-henry.father.brooklyn.map-mappoint.gif" width="405" height="320" border="0" />

Here is the satellite photo of the area.

--------
AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
TITLE: SARS Outbreak - How Bad Is It?
STATUS: publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 1
ALLOW PINGS: 1
PRIMARY CATEGORY: Misc
CATEGORY: Misc

DATE: 03/23/2003 11:00:08 PM
-----
BODY:
<font color=red><b>This page contains unconfirmed information and please take as rumor only</b></font>

SARS has been popular on the web. I have seen reports of bloggers <a href="http://www.gweilodiaries.com/archives/000728.html">here</a> and <a href="http://www.biomedcentral.com/news/20030320/09">there</a>.

Today, one of my friends, who is visiting Shanghai next week, asked me about SARS on MSN Messenger.

<blockquote>HI, am just concerned with SARS outbreak.  Is it bad in Shanghai?</blockquote>

Well. Is it bad? Actually, I didn't heard of the term SARS before. Soon I realized, via <a href="http://www.google.com/search?sourceid=navclient&ie=UTF-8&oe=UTF-8&q=sars+outbreak">Google</a>, that it is linked to the <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030212_guangzhou_virus_outbreak_pneumoniatype_.htm#000160">Pneumonia-type virus</a> <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030216_eyes_on_guangzhou.htm#000162">outbreak</a>in Guangzhou two months before.  Now it got a new name and the new location.

<blockquote>HONGKONG -- The worldwide outbreak of a mystery pneumonia is believed to have been triggered by a sick doctor from southern China who infected six other people at a Hongkong hotel, health officials said. 
Source: <a href="http://straitstimes.asia1.com.sg/latest/story/0,4390,178202-1048197540,00.html">SARS outbreak traced to HK hotel</a></blockquote>

<b>It is bad. But how bad?</b>

I am living in Shanghai. To be honest, I have never heard of any relationship between SARS and the city until I saw it in MSN Messenger. For bad news like this in China, you can never count on media to tell you the news - the main news source is still emails and Internet. But they are more like rumor than the truth. Sometimes the bad news is magnified and become worse.

The pneumonia-type virus breakout in Guangzhou two months ago was bad - really bad. People are rushing to stores to buy medicines. Most people are wearing medical masks on the streets which strengthened the anxiousness.

The following photos were taken in Guangzhou in mid-Feb this year.

<img alt="guangzhou-virus-people.jpg" src="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/2003/2/12/guangzhou-virus-people.jpg" width="334" height="500" border="0" />

<img alt="Guangzhou-Virus-waiting.jpg" src="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/2003/2/12/guangzhou-virus-street.jpg"  border="0" />

<img alt="Guangzhou-Virus-waiting.jpg" src="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/2003/2/12/Guangzhou-Virus-waiting.jpg" width="500" height="290" border="0" />

<img alt="guangzhou-sars.policy.jpg" src="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/2003/03/23/guangzhou-sars.policy.jpg" width="230" height="167" border="0" />
Policemen in Guangzhou are wearing masks. Source: Tom.com

<b>In Shanghai, so far so good</b>

In Shanghai, however, only one person died in Changzheng (Long March) Hospital (as far as I know) in Feb. -- Disclaimer: This may not be the truth since I am not sure whether the email I got is true or not. The only confirmed fact is, I received an email stating one person died for this virus in Shanghai. Please do take this as rumor.

<font color=red><b>Update</b></font> <i>March 27, 2003</i>

The city newspaper reported <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030323_sars_outbreak_how_bad_is_it.htm#000185">no case of SARS was found</a> in Shanghai on March 27, 2003 as headline news.

<b>SARS Symptoms</b>

Fever (over 38 degrees Celsius)
 - AND -
One or more respiratory symptoms including cough, shortness of breath, difficulty breathing

Refer to <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030326_sars_symptons.htm#000190">another</a> blog entry for more details.

<b>Related</b>

<ul><li><a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030212_guangzhou_virus_outbreak_pneumoniatype_.htm#000160">Pneumonia-type virus</a> outbreak in Guangzhou
<li><a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030216_eyes_on_guangzhou.htm#000162">Eyes on Guangzhou</a>
<li><a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030327_no_sars_case_found_in_shanghai.htm#000189">No SARS in Shanghai</a>, news reported.
<li><a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030326_sars_symptons.htm#000190">SARS Symptoms</a></ul>

Thanks for Mainlander's contribution. Here are some sites in Chinese about the prevention of SARS.

<ul><li><a href="http://www.chinacdc.net.cn/info/kuaixun.asp">http://www.chinacdc.net.cn/info/kuaixun.asp</a>
<li><a href="http://sc.info.gov.hk/gb/www.info.gov.hk/info/infection-c.htm">http://sc.info.gov.hk/gb/www.info.gov.hk/info/infection-c.htm</a></ul>

Visitors to Shanghai - and China in general - are either positive or negative about the place, seldom indifferent. AUTHOR: Shanghai Knight

DATE: 04/03/2003 06:22:15 PM
Update on SARS - from a friend in Singapore:

Worried About getting SARS? Take these precautions:
---------------------------------------------------

(i) Try to keep your hands away from your face.

(ii) Wash your hand often. If you go out, wash your hand when you reach home.

(iii) Soap and water are a good defence. Cornaviruses cannot withstand any 
sort of detergent.

(iv) Alcohol-based hand rubs are effective, too.

(v) Keep away from crowded areas.

Latest
------
The Strait Times, Thursday, April 3, 2002

1. The World Health Organisation (WHO) yesterday (2 April) made an 
extraordinary call on travellers to stay away from Hong Kong and 
neighbouring Guangdong province.

2. Thailand yesterday ordered all foreigners from SARS-hit countries to 
wear masks at all times or face a fine of 10,0000 baht (S$417) or up to six 
months in jail.

3. Toronto worst hit city outside Asia: Six dead.

4. Taiwan has 14 confirmed cases. 78 suspected cases.

5. WHO finally gets permission to enter worst-hit province, but SARS 
outbreak is still played down elsewhere in C66hina.

6. Statistics on China's SARS death toll:
Guangdong 46, 9 peole died there last month.

WHO revealed:
(i)   Three previously undisclosed deaths in Guangxi.

(ii)  Three SARS deaths and 11 cases in Guangxi province.

(iii)  Hunan has seven cases but no deaths.

(iv)   Shanxi, four cases and no deaths.

(v)  Sichuan, three cases and no deaths.

(vi) Unlike Guangdong, the Shanghai and Beijing authorities have chosen to 
let the issue lie low with barely any   information about SARS in the media 
or public health measures firmly put in places. Shanghai authorities 
reported its first suspected case yesterday.

Bejing Neswpaper reported 12 cases and 3 deaths.

7. Some people may become 'super-infector'. Just one person, former 
air-stewardess Esther Mok, started the chain transmission of Sars bug in 
Singapore, infecting a total of 91 people. Singapore has a total of 98 
confirmed Sars cases.

Statistics (As of Wednesday, April 2; Source: WHO website and AP).
----------

TOP 5 SARS LOCATIONS
1. China         1,190 cases 46 dead

2. Hongkong      708 cases   16 dead

3. Canada        151 cases*  6 dead
(* includes SARS patients and those who might have caught it)

4. Singapore     98 cases    4 dead

5. Vietnam       58 cases    4 dead

SARS cases have been reported from Taiwan, Thailand, Malaysia, Australia, 
New Zealand, Britain, Germany, Ireland, France, Romania, Belgium, Italy, 
and the United States.


Some Good Developments:
-----------------------
1. Singapore is expected to have a test for severe acute respiratory 
syndrome (SARS) ready in about a fortnight, which will allow doctors to 
confirm that victims actually have the virus.

Singapore General Hospital virologist Ling, Ai Ee said yesterday that the 
diagnostic tests, which are already being used on some suspected SARS 
patients here, are based on bits of DNA that are unque to the conronavirus.

2. Previously I mentioned about 'SARS vaccination', it should read 'SARS 
serum'.

In the meanwhile, doctors are still studying if it is possible to use serum 
taken from recovered patients to treat more patients here and whether it 
will work, as well as looking at the Hongkong experience to understand how 
much serum to use and when to use it.

Shanghai Knight

AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
TITLE: SARS Symptons
STATUS: publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 1
ALLOW PINGS: 1
PRIMARY CATEGORY: Misc
CATEGORY: Misc

DATE: 03/26/2003 11:54:38 PM
-----
BODY:
<b>Severe Acute Respiratory Syndrome (SARS)
Case Definitions</b>

<blockquote>Case definitions and related recommendations are subject to revision as further epidemiological/laboratory information becomes available.</blockquote>

<b>Suspect Case:</b>

A person presenting with:

Fever (over 38 degrees Celsius)

AND

One or more respiratory symptoms including cough, shortness of breath, difficulty breathing

AND

One or more of the following:

<ul><li>Close contact* within 10 days of onset of symptoms with a probable case
<li>History of travel within 10 days to WHO reported “affected areas?in Asia (see below) </ul>

AND

No other known cause of current illness

*Close contact means having cared for, lived with or had face-to-face (within 1 metre) contact with, or having had direct contact with respiratory secretions and/or body fluids of a person with SARS.

Source: <a href="http://www.hc-sc.gc.ca/pphb-dgspsp/sars-sras/sarscasedef-0317_e.html">Health Canada</a> &copy; Health Canada. 2003. Reproduce with <a href="http://www.hc-sc.gc.ca/pphb-dgspsp/notices_e.html">permission</a>.

It is REPORTED that there is no SARS case in Shanghai in the popular Shanghai Morning Post today. 

According to the speakman of Shanghai Health Administration up to now, there is no case found yet. He also mentioned some foreign media's report on infection in Shanghai is not true.

It is normal that if there is any bad news, the official will clarify the truth. I hope the report or the news I heard from my friends are just rumor. Please also treat all the information on SARS on this web site as rumor too.

P.S. I had the physical examination for driver's license today. There are many very interesting tests. I am not sure of the name in English yet.

AUTHOR: Jian Shuo Wang
TITLE: Bill Gates Murdered by Media in China
STATUS: publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 1
ALLOW PINGS: 1
PRIMARY CATEGORY: Misc
CATEGORY: Misc

DATE: 03/29/2003 01:12:22 PM
-----
BODY:
This morning, my wife received a phone call from her friend that Microsoft Chairman Bill Gates was murdered in Los Angeles. What? The whole world goes crazy!

Her friend continued to tell the bad news. She was on a taxi and the radio is repeatedly reporting the news - Microsoft Chairman Bill Gates was murdered in Los Angeles when he was attending a charity ceremony. The reporter is using very sorrow voice and interrupted the regular news. The news comes from China International Radio Station, he reported.

I was completely shocked, as much as I heard the news of Sept 11 one and a half years ago. I went to Sina.com.cn, the largest and most popular website in China, and it has put it in red font on the home page: Bill Gates Murdered in Los Angeles. The same piece of news appear on <a href="http://sohu.com">Sohu.com</a> and <a href="http://cn.yahoo.com">Yahoo! China</a> too. Here are some screen shot of the news.

<img border="2" src="http://www.wangjianshuo.com/news/20030329BillGatesMurdered/screen-tech.sina.com.cn-bill.killed.text.only.jpg" width="570" height="115">
&quot;<i>CNN: Microsoft President Bill Gates Murdered in Los Angeles</i>&quot;<i> 11:28 
AM, March 29, 2003 on Sina.com.cn</i>

<img border="2" src="http://www.wangjianshuo.com/news/20030329BillGatesMurdered/screen-cn.yahoo.com-bill.murdered.text.only.jpg" width="498" height="97">
<i>&quot;CNN: Microsoft President Bill Gates Murdered in Los Angeles</i>&quot;<i> 11:12 
AM, March 29, 2003 on Yahoo! China</i>

<a href="http://www.wangjianshuo.com/news/20030329BillGatesMurdered/screen-cn.yahoo.com.iraq-bill.killed.jpg"><img border="0" src="http://www.wangjianshuo.com/news/20030329BillGatesMurdered/screen-cn.yahoo.com.iraq-bill.killed_small.jpg" xthumbnail-orig-image="screen-cn.yahoo.com.iraq-bill.killed.jpg" width="200" height="150"></a> <a href="http://www.wangjianshuo.com/news/20030329BillGatesMurdered/screen-cn.yahoo.com-bill.murdered.jpg"><img border="0" src="http://www.wangjianshuo.com/news/20030329BillGatesMurdered/screen-cn.yahoo.com-bill.murdered_small.jpg" xthumbnail-orig-image="screen-cn.yahoo.com-bill.murdered.jpg" width="200" height="150"></a>

<a href="http://www.wangjianshuo.com/news/20030329BillGatesMurdered/screen-it.sohu.com-bill.killed.jpg"><img border="0" src="http://www.wangjianshuo.com/news/20030329BillGatesMurdered/screen-it.sohu.com-bill.killed_small.jpg" xthumbnail-orig-image="screen-it.sohu.com-bill.killed.jpg" width="200" height="144"></a> <a href="http://www.wangjianshuo.com/news/20030329BillGatesMurdered/screen-tech.sina.com.cn-bill.killed.details.jpg"><img border="0" src="http://www.wangjianshuo.com/news/20030329BillGatesMurdered/screen-tech.sina.com.cn-bill.killed.details_small.jpg" xthumbnail-orig-image="screen-tech.sina.com.cn-bill.killed.details.jpg" width="200" height="144"></a>

The words spread quickly. I got 3 phone calls and 4 MSN Messenger queries in just half hour (from 11:30 to 12:00). People are spreading the news as quick as they did when the first plane hit the NYWTC. Thanks to the morden technilogy - via <a href="http://home.wangjianshuo.com/archives/20030316_micropayment_with_mobile_sms_in_china.htm#000177">SMS</a>, mobile, and MSN Messenger. You know what, the first reaction for a lot of my friends is, forward the news to his/her friends.

On the web, it causes stronger reaction - 190 comments were posted on Sina.com.cn under the news entry. 

On the contrary, CNN.com, MSNBC, Yahoo! are just as usual - the news cannot be found there. 

After about one hour, the rumor ended. Sohu released an announcement that the 
news is fake. Sina did the same 1.5 hours later. This event raises everyone's attention to the media in China again - who is responsible for this?

<img border="1" src="http://www.wangjianshuo.com/news/20030329BillGatesMurdered/screen-news.sohu.com-bill.fake.news.PNG" width="599" height="339">
<i>Sohu IT News, March 29</i> 

<img border="1" src="http://www.wangjianshuo.com/news/20030329BillGatesMurdered/screen-tech.sina.com.cn-bill.murdered.story.PNG" width="404" height="144">
<i>Sina's clarification of the fake news, March 29</i> 

<b>Big names in this game</b>

Big names in the traditional media industry in China is involved in this game. Besides Sina and Sohu, the following agencies also reported the news:

CCTV 4 (according to posts in BBS)
China International Radio (according to my friends who heard it)
Oriental TV (according to BBS)

<b>What people are saying at hearing the news</b>

There are 190 posts under Sina.com.cn's entry. They reflect the real reaction of people when hearing the news. I digits some of them. They are all posted within 1 hour after the news is release.

<blockquote>He should be fine, from IP:210.21.107.*</blockquote>
<blockquote>What on earth is it? Is it true of false? May God Bless Bill Gates. IP:211.91.134.*</blockquote>
<blockquote>Oh, my god. It cann't be true. Why not murder Bush? Bill is a good guy! IP:218.68.239.*</blockquote>
<blockquote>Don't fool us! People who love to donote to charity will be fine. IP:202.110.116.*</blockquote>
<blockquote>It is really on China Daily. I don't know whether it is true or not. I hope it will be false. IP:61.236.192.*</blockquote>

<font color=red><b>Updated</b></font> <b>Source of the fake news</b> <i>March 31, 2003</i>

All the media pointed out that China Daily is the source of the fake news. According to an announcement later, China Daily said:

<blockquote>America news website CNN (CNN.com) reported on March 28, 2003 (Morning of March 29, 2003 Beijing time), that "Bill Gates was murdered in LA". The news appeared on CNN's web site for about half an hour before it was removed. Till now, other news media and agencies didn't report the news.

After China Daily translated and reported the news, Sina and Sohu quoted the news and spread the news via SMS. At 12:20 AM, March 29, 2003 Beijing time, Microsoft cooperation called China Daily and told us that the news is released in April 1, 2002. It appeared on CNN for unknown reason.</blockquote>
